[Modeling 3D Pedestrian-Vehicle Interactions for Vehicle-Conditioned Pose Forecasting](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08962)

- Vehicle-conditioned 3D pose forecasting: introduces a multi-agent interaction framework for predicting pedestrian skeletal motion by explicitly conditioning predictions on surrounding vehicle trajectories.
- The system employs a dedicated vehicle encoder and a Pedestrian-Vehicle Interaction Cross-Attention (PVI-CA) module to integrate historical pedestrian motion with vehicle bounding box data.
- The architecture utilizes Discrete Cosine Transform (DCT) to compress motion sequences and extends Trajectory-Aware Relative Position Encoding (TRPE) to model complex spatial-temporal relationships between agents.

---

[Digital Twin and Agentic AI for Wild Fire Disaster Management: Intelligent Virtual Situation Room](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08949)

- IVSR (Intelligent Virtual Situation Room): introduces a bidirectional Digital Twin platform for wildfire management, with Real-World Environment Assets, a Bidirectional Digital Twin, an IVSR Module, AI Agent, Disaster Simulation Library, and Human-in-the-Loop components, where the system synchronizes physical conditions with a virtual replica to automate disaster response.
- The framework utilizes a similarity engine to align real-time sensor data with a precomputed Disaster Simulation Library to generate calibrated intervention tactics.
- The architecture includes reinforcement-learning- and LLM-based agents to facilitate autonomous decision-support while maintaining expert oversight for command authorization.

---

[CoRefine: Confidence-Guided Self-Refinement for Adaptive Test-Time Compute](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08948)

- CoRefine (Confidence-Guided Self-Refinement): introduces a confidence-guided self-refinement framework with a frozen LLM, confidence extraction, temporal downsampling, a Conv1D controller, synthesis prompts, message compaction, an iterative refinement loop, and a tree structure, enabling adaptive test-time compute allocation based on token-level confidence dynamics.
- The system extracts full-trace confidence features from a frozen LLM and maps them to control actions, achieving approximately 190x token reduction compared to 512-sample parallel decoding baselines.
- It extends to CoRefine Tree, a hybrid variant that combines sequential refinement with parallel branching and early stopping to balance exploration and exploitation across mathematical reasoning benchmarks.

---

[PIXELLOG: LOGGING OF ONLINE GAMEPLAY FOR COGNITIVE RESEARCH](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08941)

- pixelLOG (Logging of Online Gameplay): introduces a high-performance, plugin-based data collection framework for Spigot-based Minecraft servers designed for process-based cognitive research, with MainController, PixelPlayer, Logger, Task Manager, PlayerStatePoller, PlayerEventListener, Logger Controller, Assembler, and Log Files.
- The system employs a hybrid approach of active state polling and passive event monitoring to capture fine-grained behavioral data at frequencies exceeding 20 updates per second.
- It facilitates robust session isolation and produces structured JSON outputs compatible with standard analytical pipelines for high-resolution analysis of cognitive processes in virtual environments.

---

[Teaching an Old Dynamics New Tricks: Regularization-free Last-iterate Convergence in Zero-sum Games via BNN Dynamics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08938)

- BNNAC (BNN Actor-Critic): introduces a regularization-free multi-agent learning framework for zero-sum games, with BNNAC (BNN Actor-Critic), actor-logits network, critic network, reach network, and softmax transformation, where the system leverages Brown-von Neumann-Nash dynamics to achieve last-iterate convergence without payoff perturbations.
- The framework achieves last-iterate convergence in zero-sum games by leveraging intrinsic BNN stability without requiring hyperparameter-sensitive regularization terms.
- It utilizes neural function approximation to scale to large extensive-form games and demonstrates superior adaptability in nonstationary environments compared to state-of-the-art regularized methods.

---

[Comparing AI Coding Agents: A Task-Stratified Analysis of Pull Request Acceptance](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08915)

- AIDev Evaluation Framework: introduces an empirical comparison of five autonomous agents using 7,156 pull requests from the AIDev dataset, with OpenAI Codex, GitHub Copilot, Devin, Cursor, Claude Code, Task-Stratified Comparison, and Temporal Trend Analysis.
- The study identifies task type as a dominant factor influencing pull request acceptance rates, showing that documentation tasks achieve significantly higher success than new feature implementations.
- Statistical analysis reveals that no single agent outperforms others across all task categories, though Devin shows the only consistent improvement in performance over time.

---

[Gesturing Toward Abstraction: Multimodal Convention Formation in Collaborative Physical Tasks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08914)

- RSA (Rational Speech Act): introduces a multimodal extension of the Rational Speech Act framework to model how agents establish linguistic and gestural conventions during repeated physical assembly tasks.
- The framework employs an Instructor agent that selects multimodal messages using a utility function that balances informativeness with the costs of speech and gesture.
- A Pragmatic Builder agent updates its belief state over a multimodal lexicon using Bayesian inference to acquire abstract tower representations and adapt to the Instructor's modality preferences.

---

[Dr. MAS: Stable Reinforcement Learning for Multi-Agent LLM Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08847)

- Dr. MAS (Stable Reinforcement Learning for Multi-Agent LLM Systems): introduces an end-to-end RL training framework for multi-agent LLM systems, with multi-agent orchestration, agent-model assignment, per-agent configuration, shared resource pooling, and an RL trainer, including verifier-, search-, answer- and solver-agents.
- The system stabilizes training by replacing global normalization with agent-wise reward statistics to calibrate gradient scales and reduce gradient-norm spikes.
- It enables co-training of heterogeneous LLMs through shared resource scheduling and flexible model-to-agent mapping.

---

[Division of labor enables efficient collective decision-making under uncertainty](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08840)

- Stochastic Foraging Model: introduces a decentralized decision-making framework where a division of labor between risk-tolerant scouts and risk-averse deliberators enables efficient collective resource acquisition, including scout- and deliberator-agents.
- Individual agents maintain a subjective belief about environmental states by observing group-wide foraging successes and failures to update their private decision thresholds.
- The research demonstrates that optimal group heterogeneity emerges under intermediate ecological pressures, with the number of exploratory scouts scaling sublinearly with population size.

---

[Taming Scylla: Understanding the multi-headed agentic daemon of the coding seas](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08765)

- Scylla: introduces an evaluation framework for benchmarking agentic coding tools through structured ablation studies across seven testing tiers, with E2E Runner, Workspace Manager, Tier Manager, Checkpoint System, Adapter Layer, Judge Pipeline, and Analysis Pipeline.
- The framework utilizes a model-agnostic adapter pattern to execute CLI-based tools and evaluates them using a multi-LLM judge consensus mechanism including Opus 4.5, Sonnet 4.5, and Haiku 4.5 models.
- It introduces the Cost-of-Pass (CoP) metric to quantify the economic trade-offs between architectural complexity and task performance in automated software development.

---

[Approximate-EFX Allocations with Ordinal and Limited Cardinal Information](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08714)

- ρ-Virtual-EFX: introduces a query-enhanced framework for approximate-EFX fair division, with ρ-Virtual-EFX, PRR, MFRR, value queries, binary search, virtual valuation functions, agent partitioning, and RoundRobin/Match&amp;Freeze subroutines, where the system achieves constant-factor fairness by eliciting limited cardinal information to augment ordinal preference rankings.
- The framework utilizes binary search and value queries to construct virtual valuation functions that serve as proxies for agents' true additive values.
- It provides near-optimal tradeoffs between the number of queries and the EFX approximation factor for general, constant-agent, and bivalued instances.

---

[LLM-Enhanced Wearables for Comprehensible Health Guidance in LMICs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08701)

- Guardian Angel: introduces an end-to-end personal wellness platform for low-resource settings, featuring a screenless wearable paired with a tiered LLM pipeline and a WhatsApp-based conversational agent.
- The architecture includes a sensor data analyzer for raw waveform interpretation, a model selector for cost-efficient routing between GPT-4o-mini, o3-mini, and o1, and a prompter analyzer for RAG-based clinical grounding.
- By offloading interpretation to the cloud and using familiar messaging interfaces, the framework overcomes barriers of digital literacy, device cost, and sensor noise to improve health data comprehension.

---

[Reasoning aligns language models to human cognition](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08693)

- Active Probabilistic Reasoning Task: introduces a mechanistic model to evaluate human-LLM alignment by disentangling sampling from inference with Evidence, Memory Update, Memory State, Strategy, Internal Posterior, Choice Biases, Occlusion Awareness, and Policy components, where latent variables characterize decision-making strategies.
- The framework utilizes a Bayesian-inspired architecture to capture deviations from optimal behavior in memory retention, decision strategy, and systematic biases.
- Results indicate that extended reasoning traces significantly improve LLM inference quality and belief trajectories, making them more human-aligned while leaving a gap in active information acquisition.

---

[SoK: The Pitfalls of Deep Reinforcement Learning for Cybersecurity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08690)

- DRL4SEC (Deep Reinforcement Learning for Cybersecurity): systematizes 11 methodological pitfalls across environment modeling, agent training, performance evaluation, and system deployment to bridge the gap between simulation and operational reality.
- The framework identifies critical issues such as incomplete MDP definitions, unaddressed partial observability, and lack of variance analysis that lead to brittle or misleading security solutions.
- Through empirical analysis of 66 papers and three case studies, the research provides actionable recommendations to mitigate performance degradation and establish methodological standards for robust DRL applications.

[6G-Bench: An Open Benchmark for Semantic Communication and Network-Level Reasoning with Foundation Models in AI-Native 6G Networks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08675)

- Standardization Collection and Task Extraction (gathering 6G standards and defining 30 tasks); Semantic State and Action Abstraction (reconstructing semantic states from mission intent and network telemetry); Benchmark Instantiation and Task Conditioning (generating task-conditioned MCQ instances for LLM evaluation); Dataset Validation (automated structural checks and expert human review); Evaluation and Metrics (calculating task-level, category-level, and stochastic pass@k accuracy)
- 6G-Bench: introduces an open benchmark for evaluating semantic communication and network-level reasoning in AI-native 6G networks, with Standardization Collection and Task Extraction, Semantic State and Action Abstraction, Benchmark Instantiation and Task Conditioning, Dataset Validation, and Evaluation and Metrics.-
- The framework evaluates 22 foundation models, including dense and mixture-of-experts architectures, across 30 decision-making tasks derived from global standardization bodies like 3GPP, IETF, and O-RAN.

[OSCAR: Optimization-Steered Agentic Planning for Composed Image Retrieval](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08603)

- OSCAR (Optimization-Steered Agentic Planning): introduces, a framework for composed image retrieval, with VLM Planner (decomposes queries and selects tools), Atomic Retrieval Construction (generates positive and negative search units), Offline Optimization (derives optimal trajectories via mixed-integer programming), Golden Library (stores trajectories for in-context demonstrations), and VLM Verifier (performs final relevance scoring), where it includes planning- and verification-agents to reformulate agentic retrieval as a trajectory optimization problem.
- The system employs an offline stage to mathematically solve for the best combination of retrieval tools and boolean set operations, storing these as "golden" demonstrations.
- During online inference, the VLM Planner retrieves similar trajectories from the library to steer its planning, achieving superior performance with minimal training data.

---

[ValueFlow: Measuring the Propagation of Value Perturbations in Multi-Agent LLM Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08567)

- ValueFlow: introduces a perturbation-based evaluation framework for measuring and analyzing value drift in multi-agent LLM systems, with Multi-Agent System, Value Measurement Dataset, LLM Value Judge, Perturbation-Based Probing, β-susceptibility, and System Susceptibility, where it quantifies the propagation of value deviations through agent interactions.
- The framework includes LLM-based agents, an LLM Value Judge, and LLM-based generators and discriminators for dataset construction.
- It identifies that structural properties like centrality and reachability amplify perturbation effects while high in-degree aggregation at sensitive nodes reduces system susceptibility.

[Homing through Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08566)

- RL (Reinforcement Learning) Homing Framework: introduces a Q-learning approach for self-propelled agents to navigate toward a target in a continuous 2D domain, with state s(t), action a(t), ε-greedy Policy, update orientation and position, cost C(t+Δt), Q-matrix, and termination check.
- The system maps angular deviation into binary states and utilizes a radial-distance-based cost function to update a 2x2 Q-matrix for optimal action selection.
- Multi-agent extensions incorporate short-range repulsive interactions, showing that collective dynamics and learned resetting strategies significantly reduce mean homing times compared to stochastic baselines.

[Agent-Supported Foresight for AI Systemic Risks: AI Agents for Breadth, Experts for Judgment](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08565)

- Agent-Supported Foresight Pipeline: introduces a scalable methodology for identifying systemic AI risks, with in-silico agents, Futures Wheel, Plurals framework, Consequence Generator, Risk Classifier, Deduplicator, and Evaluation Rubric, where LLM-based agents simulate strategic foresight to map cascading societal impacts.
- The system utilizes the Plurals framework to orchestrate an ensemble of agents with distinct personas, including brainstorming- and deduplication-agents, to generate multi-order consequences across three iterative rounds.
- It integrates automated risk classification and LLM-based deduplication to produce consolidated, non-redundant lists of potential societal and institutional threats.

[Robustness Is a Function, Not a Number: A Factorized Comprehensive Study of OOD Robustness in Vision-Based Driving](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.09018)

- Factorized OOD Framework: introduces a systematic evaluation of out-of-distribution robustness in vision-based driving by decomposing environments into five semantic axes and measuring performance under controlled k-factor perturbations.
- The study benchmarks FC, CNN, and ViT architectures, demonstrating that Vision Transformers and frozen foundation model features from DINO, CLIP, and BLIP-2 significantly enhance robustness at the cost of increased inference latency.
- It reveals that while temporal context via multi-frame inputs improves performance over simple baselines, it does not necessarily surpass optimized single-frame ViT policies in closed-loop driving tasks.

[Next-Gen CAPTCHAs: Leveraging the Cognitive Gap for Scalable and Diverse GUI-Agent Defense](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.09012)

- Next-Gen CAPTCHAs: introduces a scalable defense framework that generates interactive, procedurally-created challenges to exploit the cognitive gap between humans and GUI-enabled agents, with Data Curation Pipeline, Extended POMDP Agent Model, Real-web Evaluation Platform, Cognitive Gap Targeting, Rule-based Verifier, and Internal Workspace (memory) components.
- The system utilizes a data generation pipeline to synthesize unbounded unique instances that target specific agentic failure modes like weak spatial grounding and brittle state maintenance.
- Evaluation across frontier LLMs using Browser-Use, Claude Cowork, and CrewAI frameworks reveals that while reasoning-heavy models collapse traditional logic CAPTCHAs, they fail significantly on these interactive tasks.

[WorldArena: A Unified Benchmark for Evaluating Perception and Functional Utility of Embodied World Models](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08971)

- WorldArena: introduces a unified benchmark for systematically evaluating embodied world models across perceptual and functional dimensions, incorporating video quality metrics, embodied task utility, and human assessments.
- The framework evaluates models through three functional roles—data engine, policy evaluator, and action planner—utilizing VLM-based judges for interaction quality, perspectivity, and task success assessment.
- It proposes EWMScore, a unified metric that reveals a performance gap between visual fidelity and functional capability across 14 representative models.

[Learning to Coordinate via Quantum Entanglement in Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08965)

- Quantum Entanglement MARL Framework: introduces a decentralized coordination approach for multi-agent systems, with a quantum coordinator, local actors, and a differentiable QuantumSoftmax parameterization.
- The architecture separates joint policies into a quantum coordinator that generates correlated advice through quantum measurements and local actors that execute actions based on that advice.
- The framework enables gradient-based optimization of quantum measurements within a modified MAPPO algorithm to learn communication-free correlated policies that outperform classical shared randomness.

[Robust Sequential Learning in Random Order Networks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08953)

- Robust Sequential Learning in Random Order Networks: introduces a study on asymptotic truth learning in social networks, with Agents, Network Topology, Decision Ordering, Private Signals, Bayesian Inference, Celebrities, Guinea Pigs, BoostAgents Algorithm, and Learning Oracle, where the paper analyzes network robustness and provides algorithmic tools for designing resilient social learning structures.
- The research demonstrates that networks achieving random-order asymptotic truth learning are resilient to a bounded number of adversarial modifications.
- The proposed BoostAgents algorithm achieves a logarithmic approximation of the minimum modifications required to enable random-order learning in arbitrary networks.

[Learning the Value Systems of Societies with Preference-based Multi-objective Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08835)

- SVSL-P (Social Value System Learning with Policies): introduces an online preference-based multi-objective reinforcement learning framework that jointly learns a social grounding reward vector, a set of value systems representing societal clusters, and corresponding Pareto-optimal policies using a reward vector network, value system networks, an envelope Q-network, experience replay buffers, a preference buffer, and an EM clustering module.
- The architecture employs an Expectation-Maximization approach to iteratively assign agents to value system clusters while updating the shared reward model and weight-conditioned policy parameters.
- The framework integrates human-in-the-loop feedback through a preference buffer to refine value alignment and ensure learned behaviors generalize accurately within synthetic Markov Decision Processes.

[ON THE INEFFICIENCY OF SOCIAL LEARNING](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08812)

- Social Learning Intervention Model: introduces an analysis of learning efficiency in sequential decision-making environments using agents, a social planner, an information disclosure policy, a transfer scheme, and Bayesian belief updates.
- The study proves that for tail-regular signals, no combination of interventions can achieve efficient learning with a finite budget due to agents' strategic responses.
- The research identifies a fundamental tradeoff where providing precise social information reduces the informativeness of agent actions, hindering long-term information aggregation.

[Heterogeneous Distributed Zeroth-Order Nonconvex Optimization with Communication Compression](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08659)

- HEDZOC (Heterogeneous Distributed Zeroth-Order Compressed): introduces a distributed optimization framework for heterogeneous black-box scenarios, utilizing agents, local cost functions, a two-point zeroth-order gradient estimator, a communication compressor, auxiliary variables, primal-dual update logic, and a communication network to achieve linear speedup without requiring data homogeneity.
- The framework employs an indirect compression scheme with auxiliary variables to mitigate compression errors and reduce communication overhead while maintaining convergence in general nonconvex settings.
- It establishes the first provable linear speedup convergence rate for distributed zeroth-order optimization under data heterogeneity and compressed communication, validated through adversarial example generation experiments.

[PRISM: A Principled Framework for Multi-Agent Reasoning via Gain Decomposition](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08586)

- PRISM (Propose-Review-Integrate Synthesis for Multi-agent Reasoning): introduces a multi-agent framework that decomposes reasoning gains into exploration, information, and aggregation dimensions, and includes Proposer-, Reviewer-, Synthesizer-, and Validator-agents.
- The system utilizes role-based diversity among Proposers to maximize solution space coverage and employs a Sandbox for execution-grounded feedback.
- It implements iterative synthesis with closed-loop validation to achieve competitive performance across mathematical, coding, and function-calling benchmarks.

[Head-to-Head autonomous racing at the limits of handling in the A2RL challenge](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08571)

- TUM Autonomous Motorsport software architecture: introduces a modular, hierarchical robotics framework for high-speed autonomous racing, featuring offline optimization, multi-modal perception, and real-time trajectory planning at vehicle handling limits.
- The system integrates a novel GripMap for spatially resolved dynamic constraints and a robust EKF-based localization fusing LiDAR, RaDAR, and GNSS data to handle signal degradation.
- The architecture employs a Tube Model Predictive Controller and low-level stability systems like traction control and anti-lock braking to maintain stability during aggressive multi-vehicle maneuvers.

[Automating Computational Reproducibility in Social Science: Comparing Prompt-Based and Agent-Based Approaches](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08561)

- Automated Reproducibility Framework: introduces a comparative system for diagnosing and repairing computational research failures, with Dataset Creation, Prompt-Based Workflow, Agent-Based Workflow, and Output Validator components.
- The prompt-based workflow utilizes LLMs including GPT-4o, Gemini 2.5 Pro, and Qwen3-Coder to iteratively generate code fixes based on captured error logs and contextual metadata.
- The agent-based workflow employs autonomous agents such as OpenCode and Claude Code to interactively inspect files and re-run analyses within isolated Docker containers.

- The approach utilizes constructive design research to elicit societal values and expectations through physical prototyping and narrative-based impact analysis.
- The research identifies critical challenges in maintaining meaningful long-term engagement, establishing shared terminology between experts and the public, and translating qualitative participant input into actionable technical requirements.

[GISA: A Benchmark for General Information Seeking Assistant](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08543)

- GISA (General Information-Seeking Assistant): introduces a benchmark for evaluating LLM-driven search agents with brainstorming, query refinement, human annotation, and quality checking modules, where reasoning- and summarization-agents utilize search and browse tools, search trajectories, and system prompts to fulfill complex information needs.
- The framework integrates deep reasoning and broad information aggregation tasks with a live subset of periodically updated answers to resist data contamination.
- Evaluation of state-of-the-art LLMs and commercial systems reveals significant performance gaps compared to human search strategies, particularly in complex planning and information gathering.

[Dialogue Model Optimization via Agent Game and Adaptive Tree-based GRPO](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08533)

- AT-GRPO (Adaptive Tree-based Group Relative Policy Optimization): introduces a long-horizon reinforcement learning framework for dialogue optimization, with a two-agent game paradigm, style mimicry, termination prediction, and stage-aware tree expansion, and includes dialogue- and user-agents.
- The system employs a user agent to simulate dynamic interaction environments by learning user traits on-the-fly and providing turn-level termination probabilities as reward signals.
- The adaptive tree-based optimization limits node expansion to stage-aware ranges, reducing computational complexity to polynomial while preserving the capture of long-term conversational value.

[Decentralized Spatial Reuse Optimization in Wi-Fi: An Internal Regret Minimization Approach](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08456)

- Regret-matching (Internal Regret Minimization for Decentralized Spatial Reuse): introduces a decentralized learning algorithm for Wi-Fi Spatial Reuse optimization, with BSS Agents, Action Space, Reward Estimator, Internal Regret Matrix, Preference Vector, and Wi-Fi Environment, where agents minimize internal regret to reach Correlated Equilibria without explicit communication.
- The framework utilizes a reward estimator to calculate hypothetical gains for unplayed actions based on estimated airtime and bit rates extracted from standard tables.
- Simulation results demonstrate that this approach achieves near-optimal global performance and increased stability compared to standard external regret minimization methods like epsilon-greedy.

[When Evaluation Becomes a Side Channel: Regime Leakage and Structural Mitigations for Alignment Assessment](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08449)

- RBFT (Regime-Blind Fine-Tuning): introduces a structural intervention framework that suppresses regime-conditioned behavior in LLMs by enforcing representational invariance at decision-relevant bottlenecks via adversarial training.
- The approach utilizes a Gradient Reversal Layer to penalize the extractability of latent regime information from the final residual stream while maintaining task utility through LoRA-based fine-tuning.
- The research evaluates the mechanism on scientific sycophancy and temporal sleeper agent failure modes, demonstrating that representational invariance can act as a partial mitigation against regime-conditioned policies.

- A sequence-aware aggregation method utilizes the Longest Common Subsequence metric and a historical reputation mechanism to ensure the temporal validity of generated task sequences.

- Experimental results on the OpenClaw system demonstrate that vulnerabilities in memory retrieval and tool execution allow attack behaviors to propagate and persist across multiple interaction stages.

[On Protecting Agentic Systems’ Intellectual Property via Watermarking](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08401)

- AGENTWM: introduces a watermarking framework for protecting agentic system intellectual property by injecting verifiable signals into action trajectories using a Tool Library (repository of available external tools), Generator (mines candidate equivalent action segments), Verifier (validates functional equivalence of actions), Agentic LLM (autonomous reasoning and execution model), User ID (unique identifier for user-level traceability), Watermark Passes (sets of biased action distributions), and Statistical Verification (hypothesis testing for IP theft detection).
- The framework exploits semantic equivalence in tool execution paths to embed user-specific fingerprints that maintain statistical similarity to normal agentic behavior.
- Evaluations across three domains demonstrate high detection accuracy and resistance to removal attacks with minimal impact on agent performance.

[SCOUT-RAG: Scalable and Cost-Efficient Unifying Traversal for Agentic Graph-RAG over Distributed Domains](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08400)

- SCOUT-RAG (Scalable and COst-efficient Unifying Traversal): introduces a distributed agentic Graph-RAG framework for progressive cross-domain retrieval guided by incremental utility goals, with DRAA (estimates domain relevance tiers), PAGA (executes domain-adaptive graph retrieval), OASA (synthesizes cross-domain answers), AQAA (evaluates answer quality metrics), Strategy Selection (determines refinement mode), and an Iterative Refinement Loop (improves answers incrementally), which includes domain assessment-, partial answer generation-, synthesis- and quality assessment-agents.
- The framework utilizes a three-stage pipeline to perform training-free domain relevance estimation and adaptive local-to-global graph traversal across independent knowledge domains.
- It incorporates a closed-loop evaluation mechanism using LLM-based metrics to selectively expand domains or deepen graph exploration, reducing token consumption and latency compared to exhaustive baselines.

[Altruism and Fair Objective in Mixed-Motive Markov games](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08389)

- Fair Altruistic Markov Game: introduces a multi-agent reinforcement learning framework that replaces standard utilitarian objectives with Proportional Fairness to balance efficiency and equity.
- The approach includes Fair MAA2C and Fair MAPPO algorithms that utilize a fair advantage function to update decentralized actor and critic networks.
- Evaluation in social dilemma environments shows the method prevents inequitable role specialization while maintaining high collective rewards.

[GROUNDING GENERATIVE PLANNERS IN VERIFIABLE LOGIC: A HYBRID ARCHITECTURE FOR TRUSTWORTHY EMBODIED AI](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08373)

- VIRF (Verifiable Iterative Refinement Framework): introduces a neuro-symbolic architecture for embodied AI, with LLM Apprentice (generative task planner), Logic Tutor (symbolic verification engine), VLM-Cascade Perception (three-stage visual grounding pipeline), Traceable Axiom Synthesis (TAS) (knowledge acquisition workflow), Formal Ontology (TBox) (structured safety knowledge base), ABox (dynamic scene state representation), and Pellet Reasoner (deterministic logic inference engine), where the framework includes planning- and knowledge synthesis-agents to ground stochastic planners in verifiable logic through a pedagogical tutor-apprentice dialogue.
- The architecture utilizes a three-stage perception pipeline to generate rich semantic scene graphs and a RAG-based workflow to synthesize traceable safety axioms from real-world documentation.
- By operating under the Open-World Assumption and employing a deterministic reasoner, the system eliminates hazardous actions while providing causal feedback for plan repair.

[T2VTree: User-Centered Visual Analytics for Agent-Assisted Thought-to-Video Authoring](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08368)

- The framework utilizes a multi-agent planning system to translate natural language intent into editable executable plans, which are then materialized into modality-specific nodes for image, video, or audio generation.
- By co-locating specifications with multimodal outputs in a persistent tree structure, the system enables creators to backtrack, compare alternatives, and reuse successful partial configurations across multi-scene workflows.

[E-VAds: An E-commerce Short Videos Understanding Benchmark for MLLMs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08355)

[SHARP: Shapley Credit-based Optimization for Multi-Agent System](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08335)

- SHARP (Shapley-based Hierarchical Attribution for Reinforcement Policy): introduces a reinforcement learning framework for multi-agent systems, with a shared LLM, a planner agent, worker agents, a tool pool, a tripartite reward system, a counterfactual masking mechanism, group trajectory rollout, and SHARP optimization, where precise credit attribution stabilizes training and enhances coordination efficiency.
- The architecture utilizes counterfactual masking to isolate the causal impact of individual agents, enabling the calculation of Shapley-based marginal credits for fine-grained policy updates.
- By integrating global success signals with process-level execution validity, the system effectively filters harmful subagent interactions and improves coordination efficiency in long-horizon tasks.

[SWE Context Bench: A Benchmark for Context Learning in Coding](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08316)

- SWE-ContextBench: introduces a benchmark for evaluating experience reuse in programming agents by organizing related GitHub issues into sequences with shared context.
- The system evaluates agents using an experience pool of past trajectories and summaries across accuracy, time efficiency, and computational cost metrics.
- Findings indicate that oracle-guided summarized experience improves resolution rates and reduces runtime by over 60% on complex repository-level tasks.

[TextResNet: Decoupling and Routing Optimization Signals in Compound AI Systems via Deep Residual Tuning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08306)

- TextResNet: introduces a unified optimization framework for Compound AI Systems that decouples and routes textual gradients using residual learning principles to resolve semantic entanglement and attribution ambiguity.
- The system utilizes a forward pass with additive semantic deltas to maintain an identity highway and a backward pass with a semantic projector for causal routing of disentangled feedback.
- The framework includes forward-pass agents, a backward semantic projector, and a prompt optimizer, utilizing density-aware scheduling to prioritize optimization of system bottlenecks.

[Puda: Private User Dataset Agent for User-Sovereign and Privacy-Preserving Personalized AI](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08268)

- Puda (Private User Dataset Agent): introduces a user-sovereign architecture for privacy-preserving personalized AI, with Content Recorder, Dataset Agent, Access Control Agent, and multi-granular data levels.
- The system employs SLMs and LLMs to process raw browser logs into tiered privacy levels including Detailed Browsing History, Extracted Keywords, and Predefined Category Subsets.
- Evaluation using a Travel Planner Agent with context-analysis and plan-generation sub-agents demonstrates that deterministic category-based data sharing achieves 97.2% of the personalization performance of full history.

[When Benign Inputs Lead to Severe Harms: Eliciting Unsafe Unintended Behaviors of Computer-Use Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08235)

- AUTOELICIT: introduces an agentic framework that iteratively perturbs benign instructions using computer-use agent execution feedback to elicit severe unintended harms while maintaining realism.
- The system employs a two-stage pipeline featuring context-aware seed generation and execution-guided refinement to systematically surface long-tail safety risks in complex OS environments.
- It utilizes LLM-based evaluators to enforce constraints on benignity and realism while identifying goal-directed actions that violate core cybersecurity principles.

[SKILLRL: Evolving Agents via Recursive Skill-Augmented Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08234)

- SKILLRL: introduces a framework that bridges the gap between raw experience and policy improvement through automatic skill discovery and recursive evolution, utilizing an experience-based distillation mechanism to build a hierarchical SKILLBANK.
- The system employs a teacher model to extract general and task-specific heuristics from successful and failed trajectories, followed by a cold-start supervised fine-tuning phase to enable effective skill utilization.
- It incorporates a recursive evolution mechanism that allows the skill library to co-evolve with the agent's policy during reinforcement learning using Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO).

---

[Weak-Driven Learning: How Weak Agents make Strong Agents Stronger](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08222)

- WMSS (Weak Agents Can Make Strong Agents Stronger): introduces a post-training paradigm that leverages historical weak checkpoints to guide the optimization of stronger LLMs through logit mixing and curriculum-based data activation.
- The framework utilizes a three-stage pipeline involving initialization, entropy-driven data selection, and joint training to overcome performance saturation in standard supervised fine-tuning.
- By reintroducing probability mass to plausible but incorrect tokens identified by the weak agent, the system reactivates informative learning signals and refines decision boundaries without additional inference costs.

[Fork, Explore, Commit: OS Primitives for Agentic Exploration](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08199)

- Branch Context: introduces a new operating system abstraction for AI agents to perform parallel exploration with isolated filesystem and process states, utilizing a Parent Process, the branch() syscall, Child Processes, Mount Namespaces, BranchFS (FUSE), Delta Layers, and a Base Directory.
- The branch() syscall manages atomic creation of multiple child processes with kernel-enforced isolation and a first-commit-wins resolution policy.
- BranchFS provides a FUSE-based filesystem that implements file-level copy-on-write semantics and atomic commit/rollback capabilities for agent workspaces.

[Dreaming in Code for Curriculum Learning in Open-Ended Worlds](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08194)

- DiCode (Dreaming in Code): introduces an Unsupervised Environment Design framework that leverages LLMs to synthesize executable environment code, creating a structured curriculum for agents in complex open-ended worlds.
- The architecture employs a dual-stage generation cycle including task-designing and code-generation LLM components to translate conceptual goals into executable Python scripts.
- By maintaining a closed-loop curriculum grounded in agent competence, the framework enables the acquisition of long-horizon skills and late-game progression that standard reinforcement learning baselines fail to achieve.

#### 8th February 2026

[DIAL-SUMMER: A Structured Evaluation Framework of Hierarchical Errors in Dialogue Summaries](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08149)

- DIAL-SUMMER (Dialogue-Summary Errors): introduces a structured evaluation framework for dialogue summarization, featuring a hierarchical error taxonomy, a human-annotated inference dataset, and an assessment of LLM-Judges' error detection capabilities.
- The taxonomy distinguishes between dialogue-level errors, such as speaker misattribution and viewpoint distortion, and within-turn errors like changed meaning or extrinsic context hallucinations.
- Experimental results demonstrate that while LLM-Judges struggle with fine-grained error detection, providing the structured taxonomy in prompts significantly improves their performance in identifying hallucinations and incompleteness.

[Test vs Mutant: Adversarial LLM Agents for Robust Unit Test Generation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08146)

- AdverTest: introduces a mutation-guided adversarial framework for unit test generation, with Agent T (generates/refines unit test cases), Agent M (creates context-aware code mutants), Adversarial Loop (manages iterative agent interaction), Mutation Testing (calculates coverage and mutation scores), Test Suite Augmentation (targets surviving mutants with tests), Mutant Augmentation (exploits test suite blind spots), and Test-Repair Loop (ensures syntactically valid tests), where the system employs two LLM agents in a bidirectional feedback loop to co-evolve test coverage and bug detection capability.
- The framework includes a test case generation- and a mutant generation-agent that engage in an adversarial loop guided by structural coverage and mutation score feedback.
- Evaluation on real-world Java benchmarks shows that AdverTest outperforms existing search-based and LLM-driven tools in fault detection rate while producing human-readable and compilable unit tests.

[Interpretable Failure Analysis in Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08104)

- Two-stage gradient-based framework: introduces a forensic approach for Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning (MARL) that identifies the root cause of failures (Patient-0) and maps propagation pathways using policy-gradient Taylor-errors and critic-based geometric analysis.
- The system utilizes a two-stage process where Stage 1 detects local policy instability through curvature probes in observation space, while Stage 2 validates these findings by tracing accelerating upstream influence via directional second-order critic derivatives.
- The framework generates interpretable contagion graphs that quantify influence strength, amplification frequency, and propagation timing, achieving high accuracy in identifying initial failure sources across complex environments like StarCraft II.

[From Stochastic Shocks to Macroscopic Tails: The Moyal Distribution as a Unified Framework for Epidemic Dynamics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08101)

- Moyal-SIR (Stochastic Moyal-SIR Unified Framework): introduces a unified epidemiological framework that bridges microscopic agent-based simulations with macroscopic wave decomposition using the Moyal distribution to characterize extreme volatility and heavy-tailed superspreading events.
- The framework resolves the "Statistical Gap" between deterministic averages and realized risk by modeling infectiousness as a stochastic variable driven by collision dynamics rather than a constant population parameter.
- It applies spectral decomposition to multi-year pandemic data to identify distinct variant-driven waves and quantifies containment effectiveness through the emergent "Social Friction" width parameter.

[Objective Decoupling in Social Reinforcement Learning: Recovering Ground Truth from Sycophantic Majorities](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08092)

- ESA (Epistemic Source Alignment): introduces a robust reinforcement learning framework that recovers latent ground truth by auditing evaluator reliability against sparse internal axioms to prevent objective decoupling in biased social environments.
- The architecture employs an epistemic source adjudication module that utilizes Multiplicative Weights Update to dynamically suppress feedback from sycophantic or adversarial majorities.
- By filtering corrupted social signals before policy integration, the agent maintains alignment with true objectives even when the majority of feedback sources are untrustworthy.

[Spectral Guardrails for Agents in the Wild: Detecting Tool Use Hallucinations via Attention Topology](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08082)

- Spectral Guardrails: introduces a training-free safety mechanism for LLM agents that detects tool-use hallucinations by analyzing the spectral topology of attention matrices, with Transformer, Graph Laplacian, Spectral Diagnostics, and Guardrail components, where topological features are extracted from attention graphs to identify incoherent reasoning states.
- The system transforms attention weights into graph Laplacians to compute diagnostics like Smoothness and Spectral Entropy, identifying thermodynamic state changes during model errors.
- Evaluation across multiple architectures reveals that larger models exhibit distinct failure geometries, enabling single-layer spectral features to achieve high recall in detecting fabricated tool calls.

[GRAPH-ENHANCED DEEP REINFORCEMENT LEARNING FOR MULTI-OBJECTIVE UNRELATED PARALLEL MACHINE SCHEDULING](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08052)

- PPO-GNN (Proximal Policy Optimization - Graph Neural Network): introduces a deep reinforcement learning framework for the Unrelated Parallel Machine Scheduling Problem (UPMSP) that integrates a heterogeneous GNN for state representation with a PPO agent to learn direct scheduling policies.

- The architecture utilizes a GATv2-based GNN encoder to capture complex relationships between jobs, machines, and setup states, feeding into separate actor and critic MLP heads.

- The framework optimizes conflicting objectives of Total Weighted Tardiness and Total Setup Time through a multi-objective reward function and action masking for feasibility.

[Implicit Strategic Optimization: Rethinking Long-Horizon Decision-Making in Adversarial Poker Environments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08041)

- ISO (Implicit Strategic Optimization): introduces a prediction-aware framework for long-horizon adversarial games that factorizes strategic complexity into forecasting latent contexts and learning regime-conditioned policies.

- The system utilizes a Strategic Reward Model (SRM) to estimate long-term value and an iso-grpo learning rule to update context-specific policy instances based on predicted and realized strategic regimes.

- Theoretical analysis proves sublinear contextual regret scaling with mispredictions, while experiments in poker and Pokémon demonstrate superior long-term returns compared to standard LLM and RL baselines.

[DeltaKV: Residual-Based KV Cache Compression via Long-Range Similarity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.08005)

- This approach reduces KV cache memory to 29% of its original size while maintaining near-lossless accuracy and achieving up to 2x throughput improvement in long-context LLM deployment.

[CausalArmor: Efficient Indirect Prompt Injection Guardrails via Causal Attribution](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.07918)

- Experimental results on Barcelona city instances show that hybrid quantum annealing provides near-optimal solutions with superior scalability compared to classical heuristics as fleet sizes increase to 10,000 vehicles.

[DreamDojo: A Generalist Robot World Model from Large-Scale Human Videos](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06949)

- DreamDojo: introduces a foundation world model for generalist robots, utilizing Human Video Pretraining Stage (Learns physical knowledge), Robot Post-Training Stage (Adapts to target robots), Autoregressive Distillation Pipeline (Enables real-time inference), Continuous Latent Actions (Unified proxy actions), Latent Action Model (Encodes/decodes actions), Cosmos-Predict2.5 (Latent video diffusion model), DreamDojo Teacher (Bidirectional attention model), DreamDojo Student (Causal attention model), and Value Model (Estimates subtask completion), designed to simulate dexterous robotics tasks and generalize to unseen scenarios.
- The model is pretrained on DreamDojo-HV, the largest and most diverse egocentric human video dataset (44k hours), using continuous latent actions as unified proxy labels to enhance knowledge transfer and action controllability.
- A distillation pipeline accelerates the model to real-time speed (10.81 FPS) for applications including live teleoperation, policy evaluation, and model-based planning, demonstrating strong generalization in out-of-distribution tasks.

[Identification and Estimation of Network Models with Nonparametric Unobserved Heterogeneity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06885)

- NME-NUH: introduces a semiparametric dyadic network model with nonparametric unobserved heterogeneity, allowing the fixed effects to interact via an unknown coupling function $g(\cdot, \cdot)$.
- The approach identifies agents with similar unobserved fixed effects ($\xi_i = \xi_j$) using a pseudo-distance metric ($d_{ij}^2$) derived from estimated error-free outcomes ($Y_{ij}^*$).
- The parameter of interest ($\beta_0$) is estimated using a kernel-based estimator that weights pairwise-difference regressions based on the estimated pseudo-distances, ensuring consistency even with low-rank regressors and non-differentiable coupling functions.

[AIRS-Bench: a Suite of Tasks for Frontier AI Research Science Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06855)

- AIRS-BENCH (AI Research Science Benchmark): introduces a suite of 20 diverse, non-contaminated tasks sourced from state-of-the-art machine learning papers to rigorously evaluate LLM agents across the full research lifecycle. 
- The benchmark assesses agentic capabilities, requiring agents to generate code to train and validate ML models without providing baseline solutions or direct inference access. 
- An agent is defined as an LLM combined with a Scaffold (Greedy, One-Shot, or ReAct), instantiated within a Harness (AIRA-DOJO or MLGYM) that manages execution within a constrained Environment.

[Agentic Uncertainty Reveals Agentic Overconfidence](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06948)

- Agentic Uncertainty Regimes: introduces a study evaluating LLM agents' ability to predict task success (P(IS)) across four execution stages, revealing systematic agentic overconfidence.
- The study finds that pre-execution assessment often yields better discrimination than standard post-execution review, despite having strictly less information.
- Adversarial prompting, which reframes assessment as bug-finding, achieves the best calibration by reducing overconfidence by up to 15 percentage points.

[Distributed Knowledge in Simplicial Models](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06945)

- SM (Simplicial Models): introduces a framework connecting distributed computing, epistemic logic, and topology by modeling multi-agent epistemic situations using chromatic simplicial complexes, where agents' local states are vertices and global states are simplexes.
- The approach focuses on distributed knowledge, common distributed knowledge, and their geometric interpretation related to higher-dimensional connectivity within the simplicial complex structure.
- The paper applies SM to analyze the solvability of the majority consensus task in three communication models: unreliable broadcast, immediate snapshot, and test-and-set, using logical obstruction formulas.

[Implementing Grassroots Logic Programs with Multiagent Transition Systems and AI](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06934)

- madGLP (Multiagent Deterministic GLP): introduces implementation-ready operational semantics for multiagent GLP, utilizing local variable pairs connected by global links, managed via a Global Writers Table and `global_send` goals.
- The development process employs a three-layer abstraction—mathematical specification, English+code informal specification derived by AI, and final Dart code—to ensure correctness and consistency.
- The framework proves the correctness of the deterministic implementations (dGLP and madGLP) against their abstract counterparts (GLP and maGLP) using simulation relations and commutativity properties.

[Topological Semantics for Common Inductive Knowledge](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06927)

- Topological Semantics for Common Inductive Knowledge: introduces a formal logic and topological semantics for common inductive knowledge, defining agents by their information bases and switching tolerances, drawing insights from learning theory.
- The framework defines epistemic modalities using topological concepts like $n$-open and $n$-closed sets, relating an agent's ability to limit decide a proposition to its switching tolerance $n_i$ and the set's topological complexity.
- The logic is applied to solve an inductive variant of the coordinated attack problem, showing that the success sets of attestation protocols correspond precisely to non-empty $(n_i+1)$-open subsets of the proposition $P$ in the agent's topology.

[Strategizing at Speed: A Learned Model Predictive Game for Multi-Agent Drone Racing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06925)

- LMPG (Learned Model Predictive Game): introduces a method that efficiently solves dynamic games online by leveraging an amortized game formulation to accelerate computation for multi-agent drone racing.
- The LMPG approach utilizes a structured neural network trained offline to predict Nash strategies, significantly reducing the high computational latency associated with traditional Model Predictive Game (MPG) planners.
- Experiments demonstrate that LMPG outperforms both MPG and Model Predictive Control (MPC) in high-speed asynchronous racing scenarios by achieving a better trade-off between solve time and solution accuracy.

[From Kepler to Newton: Inductive Biases Guide Learned World Models in Transformers](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06923)

- IBGLWM in Transformers: introduces three minimal inductive biases—spatial smoothness, spatial stability, and temporal locality—to enable generic Transformers to learn Newtonian world models for planetary motion, overcoming prior failures of generic models.
- Spatial smoothness and stability fix issues related to tokenization and error accumulation in continuous regression, while temporal locality (context length 2) forces the model to abandon curve-fitting (Keplerian model) and discover force representations (Newtonian model).
- The results demonstrate that simple architectural choices, specifically context length, determine whether an AI system acts as a curve-fitter or a physicist, marking a critical step toward automated scientific discovery.

[TraceCoder: A Trace-Driven Multi-Agent Framework for Automated Debugging of LLM-Generated Code](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06875)

- TraceCoder: introduces a trace-driven multi-agent framework for automated debugging of LLM-generated code, emulating expert human debugging workflows using Instrumentation, Analysis, and Repair Agents, supported by HLLM and RM.
- The framework first uses the Instrumentation Agent to insert diagnostic probes, enabling the TraceRunner to capture fine-grained runtime traces for deep insight into internal execution.
- The Analysis Agent performs causal reasoning on these traces, informed by the HLLM which learns from prior failures, while the RM ensures stable convergence by reverting failed attempts to the best known correct state.

[From Features to Actions: Explainability in Traditional and Agentic AI Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06841)

- MEP (Minimal Explanation Packet): introduces a unified framework for explainability across static and agentic AI paradigms, contrasting feature attribution with trajectory-level diagnostics.
- The framework formalizes the shift from single input-output explanations to trajectory-level accounts grounded in execution context and verification signals.
- Empirical results show that trace-grounded rubric analysis reliably localizes execution-level failures in LLM agents, unlike traditional attribution methods which only capture aggregate correlations.

[LLM Active Alignment: A Nash Equilibrium Perspective](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06836)

- LLM Active Alignment (LAA): introduces a game-theoretic framework for predicting and steering the behavior of LLM populations through Nash Equilibrium analysis, where LLM agents strategically choose alignment targets as mixtures over human subpopulations.
- The approach models LLM strategies as low-dimensional convex weight vectors over subpopulation models, enabling tractable closed-form NE characterizations derived from concave games for system-level prediction and governance.
- Experiments in a social media setting demonstrate that strategic interaction can lead to political exclusion of certain subpopulations, which can be mitigated by tuning diversity incentives via the framework's utility scaling factors.

[ScaleEnv: Scaling Environment Synthesis from Scratch for Generalist Interactive Tool-Use Agent Training](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06820)

- ScaleEnv: introduces a framework for fully automated synthesis of high-fidelity, interactive, and verifiable environments and tasks for generalist tool-use agent training.
- The framework operates in two synergistic phases: Domain Foundation, which builds executable tools and databases validated via procedural testing, and Task Construction, which uses a dependency-aware graph expansion strategy.
- ScaleEnv enables agents trained via Zero RL to achieve significant zero-shot generalization on unseen, out-of-distribution benchmarks, confirming that scaling environmental diversity is critical for robust agent learning.

[Bridging 6G IoT and AI: LLM-Based Efficient Approach for Physical Layer's Optimization Tasks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06819)

- PE-RTFV (Prompt-Engineering-based Real-Time Feedback and Verification): introduces an iterative, lightweight framework for physical-layer optimization in 6G IoT networks using two specialized LLMs guided by real-time system feedback.
- The framework employs an Optimizer LLM (O-LLM) to generate structured prompts and evaluate solutions, and an Agent LLM (A-LLM) to produce task-specific actions, mimicking a gradient-descent optimization process.
- PE-RTFV is validated on a wireless-powered IoT constellation design task, achieving performance comparable to a genetic algorithm using only minimal feedback and without explicit knowledge of the energy-harvesting model.

---

[Fair Transit Stop Placement: A Clustering Perspective and Beyond](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06776)

- TrSP (Transit Stop Placement Problem): introduces a model for fair transit stop placement in general metric spaces, investigating fairness through justified representation (JR) and core stability, and proposing three algorithms: GC-TrSP, ECA, and $\lambda$-Hybrid.
- The Expanding Cost Algorithm (ECA) achieves a tight $(1+\sqrt{2})$-JR approximation, outperforming clustering-based methods like GC-TrSP, but fails to guarantee bounded core approximation, leading to the $\lambda$-Hybrid algorithm for tunable JR/Core trade-offs.
- The work establishes formal connections between TrSP and fair centroid clustering, demonstrating that clustering algorithms cannot guarantee better than 3-JR approximation in general metric spaces, highlighting the necessity of the novel ECA approach.

---

[Semantically Labelled Automata for Multi-Task Reinforcement Learning with LTL Instructions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06746)

- SEMLTL (Semantically Labelled Automata for Multi-Task Reinforcement Learning with LTL Instructions): introduces novel task embeddings based on semantic LTL-to-automata translations, enabling efficient on-the-fly computation and expressive task embeddings for conditioning a universal policy.
- The approach utilizes Limit-deterministic Büchi Automata (LDBA) states annotated with semantic labelling (Main and Breakpoint formulae) to capture task progress and memory requirements for full Linear Temporal Logic (LTL) specifications.
- The policy architecture is a multi-headed neural network that processes the MDP state via a State Encoder and the semantic embedding via a Shared Representation MLP to output a hybrid action distribution over MDP and $\epsilon$-actions.

---

[ClassAid: A Real-time Instructor-AI-Student Orchestration System for Classroom Programming Activities](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06734)

- ClassAid: introduces a real-time orchestration system that integrates a TA Agent (Six-stage orchestration pipeline) and an Instructor Dashboard (Real-time monitoring) to provide personalized, dynamically adjustable AI support for programming activities.
- The core TA Agent Backend (LLM) utilizes a six-stage framework grounded in formative and dynamic assessment theories to monitor student behavior, diagnose cognitive states, and select adaptive feedback modes (Heuristic, Technical, Auto, Silent).
- The system enables instructors to maintain pedagogical control by dynamically adjusting the LLM-based TA Agent's feedback modes in real time based on dashboard insights into student progress and AI interactions.

---

[PAIRWISE IS NOT ENOUGH: HYPERGRAPH NEURAL NETWORKS FOR MULTI-AGENT PATHFINDING](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06733)

- HMAGAT (Hypergraph Multi-Agent Attention Network): introduces a novel imitation learning framework for Multi-Agent Path Finding (MAPF) that leverages Hypergraph Neural Networks (HGNNs) to model higher-order group interactions, outperforming state-of-the-art GNN-based models.
- The architecture consists of a CNN encoder, HGNN layers, and an MLP decoder, supported by dynamic hypergraph generation strategies (k-means, Lloyd, shortest distance) and an RL-trained temperature sampling module.
- HMAGAT achieves state-of-the-art performance in learning-based MAPF solvers despite using significantly fewer parameters and less training data than previous large models, demonstrating the importance of appropriate inductive biases.

---

[Wasserstein Distributionally Robust Performative Prediction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06730)

- DR-PP (Distributionally Robust Performative Prediction): introduces a distributionally robust performative prediction framework using a decision-dependent Wasserstein ambiguity set centered on the empirical distribution to optimize the prediction model over worst-case risk.
- The framework reformulates the intractable robust objective into a computationally tractable min-max optimization problem via Lagrangian relaxation and strong duality.
- The paper develops two iterative algorithms, DR-RRM and DR-RGD, which are proven to converge linearly to a unique robust performative stable point or its bounded neighborhood under approximation errors.

---

[Table-as-Search: Formulate Long-Horizon Agentic Information Seeking as Table Completion](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06724)

- TaS (Table-as-Search): introduces a structured planning framework that reformulates long-horizon Information Seeking (InfoSeeking) as a Table Completion task, utilizing a multi-agent system centered around a shared database.
- The framework employs a Planner Main-Agent to orchestrate Dynamic Orchestration, including Row Expansion (candidate discovery) and Cell Population (information collection) via parallel Sub-Agents, managing search states precisely.
- By offloading massive search results to the external database, TaS alleviates the LLM agent's context burden, demonstrating superior robustness and efficiency across Deep, Wide, and DeepWide Search benchmarks.

---

[PrefIx: Understand and Adapt to User Preference in Human-Agent Interaction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06714)

- PrefIx: introduces a configurable environment for evaluating LLM-based agents on aligning human interaction preferences, utilizing Task Coarsening (Rewrite prompts), Preference-Aware User Simulation (Implicit preference expression), Interaction-as-a-Tool (IaaT) (Structured tool calls), and User Experience (UX) Judge (Composite LLM-as-a-Judge).
- The core Interaction-as-a-Tool (IaaT) paradigm formalizes interaction behaviors, such as confirmation requests and transparency, as structured tool calls, enabling quantitative benchmarking of agent alignment across 14 preference attributes.
- Evaluation relies on a composite LLM-as-a-Judge mechanism assessing seven UX dimensions and Interaction Preference Alignment, achieving strong aggregate reliability (ICC > 0.79) and human correlation (p = 0.52–0.78).

---

[Future-blindness and the product topology](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06672)

- Topological Characterization of Future-blindness: introduces N-blindness (Fixed future neglect) and Eventual Blindness (Endogenous future neglect) to study preferences that heavily discount the future within infinite consumption streams.
- The paper demonstrates that the finest locally convex topology ensuring eventual blindness ($\tau^b$) coincides with the product topology ($\tau^P$), providing a behavioral foundation for product topology continuity.
- N-blindness is characterized by continuity with respect to the non-Hausdorff topology $\tau^N$, and the dual spaces for $\tau^N$ and $\tau^b$ are characterized as $c^N_{\infty}$ and $c_{00}$, respectively.

---

[Two-stage stochastic algorithm for solving large-scale (non)-convex separable optimization problems under affine constraints](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06637)

- Two-stage stochastic algorithm: introduces a method for solving large-scale separable optimization problems by combining a Stochastic Dual Subgradient Algorithm and a Block-Coordinate Frank-Wolfe Algorithm.
- The approach achieves an $\epsilon$-optimal primal solution in expectation with a total complexity of $O(1/\epsilon^2 + N/\epsilon^{2/3})$ calls to the Fenchel conjugate oracle, significantly improving upon the $O(N/\epsilon^2)$ complexity of the deterministic dual subgradient method.
- The framework is extended to nonconvex problems, where the second stage uses the BCFW output and a Carathéodory decomposition to recover duality gap bounds based on the Shapley-Folkman theorem.

---

[Sample-Efficient Policy Space Response Oracles with Joint Experience Best Response](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06599)

- JBR (Joint Experience Best Response): introduces a modification to PSRO that improves sample efficiency by collecting trajectories once under the current meta-strategy profile and reusing this joint dataset to compute best responses for all agents simultaneously.
- The approach converts best response computation into an offline reinforcement learning problem, mitigating distribution-shift bias using variants like Conservative JBR, Exploration-Augmented JBR, and Hybrid BR.
- Exploration-Augmented JBR with targeted perturbation (JBR-PSRO-ST) achieves the best accuracy-efficiency trade-off, while Hybrid BR variants approach standard PSRO accuracy at reduced sample cost.

---

[AgentStepper: Interactive Debugging of Software Development Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06593)

- AgentStepper: introduces the first interactive debugger for LLM-based software development agents, enabling developers to inspect, control, and manipulate agent trajectories via a user interface, a backend, and an API.
- The system represents agent trajectories as structured conversations between the agent program, LLMs, and tools, supporting breakpoints, stepwise execution, and live editing of prompts and tool calls.
- AgentStepper tracks intermediate repository-level code changes using a version control system (git) and utilizes an LLM to summarize voluminous event information for improved readability.

---

[The Impossibility of Strategyproof Rank Aggregation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06582)

- Impossibility Theorem for Strategyproof Rank Aggregation: introduces a sweeping impossibility result showing that no anonymous SWF satisfies strategyproofness and unanimity when four or more alternatives exist.
- The research establishes an analogue of the Gibbard-Satterthwaite theorem for rank aggregation, demonstrating that strategyproofness is incompatible with basic fairness axioms.
- The main theorem is proven via SAT solving, a computer-aided theorem proving technique, and verified using the interactive proof assistant Isabelle/HOL.

---

[The Law of Task-Achieving Body Motion: Axiomatizing Success of Robot Manipulation Actions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06572)

- Law of Task-Achieving Body Motion: introduces an axiomatic correctness specification for robot manipulation actions, utilizing Scoped TEE Classes and Semantic Digital Twins (SDTs) to verify success via three predicates: SatisfiesRequest, Causes, and CanPerform.
- This framework decomposes task achievement into semantic correctness, causal sufficiency under scoped physics, and embodiment feasibility, providing a reusable, implementation-independent interface for motion synthesis and verification.
- The Law supports typed failure diagnosis (semantic, causal, embodiment, out-of-scope), feasibility analysis across different robots and environments, and counterfactual reasoning.

---

[SeeUPO: Sequence-Level Agentic-RL with Convergence Guarantees](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06554)

- SeeUPO (Sequence-level Sequential Update Policy Optimization): introduces a critic-free approach with convergence guarantees for multi-turn LLM agent interactions by modeling them as sequentially executed multi-agent bandit problems.
- The approach utilizes a reverse-order sequential policy update mechanism, leveraging backward induction to ensure monotonic improvement and convergence to the globally optimal solution.
- SeeUPO employs GRAE for joint advantage estimation and PPO-style clipping for policy updates, demonstrating superior training stability and performance on AppWorld and BFCL v4 benchmarks compared to backbone RL algorithms.

---

[Malicious Agent Skills in the Wild: A Large-Scale Security Empirical Study](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06547)

- Malicious Agent Skill Detection Pipeline: introduces the first large-scale labeled dataset of malicious agent skills by behaviorally verifying 98,380 skills, confirming 157 malicious skills with 632 vulnerabilities, using Data Collection (Gathering skills), Static Analysis (Candidate identification), Dynamic Verification (Behavioral confirmation), Manual Annotation (Vulnerability labeling), Ground-Truth Dataset (Confirmed malicious skills), Attack Archetype Analysis (Identifying strategies), and Responsible Disclosure (Ecosystem impact).
- The pipeline reveals that malicious skills average 4.03 vulnerabilities across a median of 3 kill chain phases, indicating systematic technique layering rather than accidental inclusion.
- The study identifies two negatively correlated attack archetypes: Data Thieves (supply chain exfiltration) and Agent Hijackers (instruction manipulation), with evasion scaling monotonically with attacker sophistication.

---

[AgentCPM-Report: Interleaving Drafting and Deepening for Open-Ended Deep Research](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06540)

- AgentCPM-Report (WARP: Writing As Reasoning Policy): introduces a lightweight, local deep research system built on an 8B-parameter agent that uses WARP to dynamically interleave Evidence-Based Drafting (writing content) and Reasoning-Driven Deepening (updating the dynamic outline).
- WARP models deep research as an iterative refinement loop, enabling planning decisions to emerge and adapt to the writing process itself, thereby overcoming the insight ceiling of static plan-then-write paradigms.
- The system is trained using a Multi-Stage Agentic Training strategy, including Cold Start, Atomic Skill RL, and Holistic Pipeline RL, to ensure stable convergence and high performance despite using a small-scale LLM.

---

[COMPLETING MISSING ANNOTATION: MULTI-AGENT DEBATE FOR ACCURATE AND SCALABLE RELEVANCE ASSESSMENT FOR IR BENCHMARKS](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06526)

- DREAM (Debate-based RElevance Assessment with Multi-agents): introduces a multi-agent debate framework using LLM agents with opposing initial stances and iterative reciprocal critique to achieve high-accuracy relevance labeling and reliable AI-to-human escalation.
- The framework automatically annotates cases where agents agree and escalates genuinely uncertain cases (persistent disagreement) to human annotators, leveraging the debate history as a supportive resource.
- Using DREAM, the authors construct BRIDGE, a refined Information Retrieval (IR) benchmark that mitigates evaluation bias by uncovering 29,824 missing relevant chunks in existing datasets.

---

[Evolutionary Generation of Multi-Agent Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06511)

- EvoMAS (Evolutionary Generation of Multi-Agent Systems): introduces a configuration-based evolutionary framework that automatically synthesizes robust Multi-Agent Systems (MAS) by iteratively refining structured configurations using LLM-guided selection, mutation, crossover, and memory.
- The framework represents MAS designs as declarative configurations defining agent roles, backbone models, tool access, and communication topology, which are executed by a lightweight runtime interpreter.
- EvoMAS consistently outperforms human-designed MAS and prior automatic MAS generation methods across reasoning, coding, and tool-use benchmarks, achieving high execution reliability and discovering novel coordination patterns.

---

[JADE: Expert-Grounded Dynamic Evaluation for Open-Ended Professional Tasks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06486)

- JADE (Judge Agents with Dynamic Evaluation): introduces a two-layer evaluation framework for open-ended professional tasks, including Expert-Authored Evaluation Skills, Checklist Generator (LLM), Query-Specific Checklist, Report-Specific Checklist, Extracted Claims, Verification Agent, LLM Judge, Dependency Gating, and Aggregate Scoring.
- JADE resolves the stability-adaptivity dilemma by decoupling domain-general evaluation principles (Layer 1) from case-specific evidence verification (Layer 2), ensuring stable, expert-grounded, and adaptive assessment.
- The framework employs a two-track scoring mechanism where factual claims are validated by a Verification Agent via real-time web search, and reasoning is assessed by an LLM Judge, with Dependency Gating ensuring soundness.

---

[AgentCPM-Explore: Realizing Long-Horizon Deep Exploration for Edge-Scale Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06485)

- AgentCPM-Explore: introduces a compact 4B agent model designed for long-horizon deep exploration, utilizing parameter-space model merging, reward signal denoising, and contextual information refinement to overcome small model training challenges.
- The system employs a comprehensive three-stage training framework, including AgentRL for fully asynchronous reinforcement learning and AgentDock for standardized tool and sandbox management.
- By addressing catastrophic forgetting, reward noise sensitivity, and context contamination, AgentCPM-Explore achieves state-of-the-art performance among 4B-class models, demonstrating the potential of edge-scale LLMs.

---

[Prism: Spectral Parameter Sharing for Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06476)

- Prism: introduces a spectral parameter sharing framework for Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning (MARL) that induces inter-agent diversity by decomposing shared network weights using SVD and applying agent-specific spectral masks to the singular values.
- The framework shares singular vector directions (U, V) among all agents while allowing each agent to learn distinct spectral masks ($\Sigma_i$) applied to the singular values, balancing commonality and specialization.
- Prism achieves competitive performance and superior resource efficiency compared to existing MARL parameter sharing methods by operating solely in the compact spectral space, mitigating the trade-off between scalability and policy heterogeneity.

---

[Distributed Circumferential Coverage Control in Non-Convex Annulus Environments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06472)

- Distributed Circumferential Coverage Control (DCCC): introduces a distributed coverage control formulation for multi-agent systems operating in non-convex annulus environments, utilizing Virtual Partition Bars and Partition Dynamics for workload equalization.
- The approach constructs a Riemannian metric to enable agent navigation within non-convex subregions while guaranteeing collision avoidance with region boundaries.
- Theoretical analysis confirms the exponential convergence of workload partition and asymptotic convergence of agents toward their local optimal positions.

---

[User-Centric Object Navigation: A Benchmark with Integrated User Habits for Personalized Embodied Object Search](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06459)

- UcON (User-centric Object Navigation Benchmark): introduces a novel evaluation framework for personalized embodied object search, integrating user habits via a User Habit Knowledge Base and evaluating agents using components like the Habit Retrieval Module, Object Detector, Foundation LLM, and Low-level Planner.
- The benchmark features 489 distinct object categories and over 22,600 human-object habits, shifting the focus from general scene priors to personalized object placement tendencies.
- The proposed Habit Retrieval Module (HRM) enhances LLM reasoning by selectively retrieving task-relevant habits from the large knowledge base to mitigate performance degradation caused by long prompts.

[Principle-Evolvable Scientific Discovery via Uncertainty Minimization](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06448)

- PIEVO: introduces a framework that reformulates scientific discovery as Bayesian optimization over an evolving principle space, utilizing a multi-agent system guided by dynamic principle refinement and anomaly-driven augmentation.
- The framework employs Information-Directed Selection (IDS) and Gaussian Process (GP) experts to balance exploration and exploitation, achieving superior sample efficiency and theoretical sublinear cumulative regret.
- PIEVO achieves state-of-the-art solution quality (up to 93.15%) across four diverse scientific benchmarks, demonstrating robustness and the capacity to uncover novel physical laws.
