[TrajAD: Trajectory Anomaly Detection for Trustworthy LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06443)

- TrajAD: introduces a specialized auditing framework for runtime Trajectory Anomaly Detection, verifying LLM agent execution traces using a Check-and-Act protocol and enabling efficient Rollback-and-Retry error recovery.
- The framework utilizes TrajBench, a large-scale dataset synthesized via a Perturb-and-Complete strategy, to train the verifier for precise anomaly detection and error step localization.
- TrajAD models the global context of execution traces to distinguish between normal and anomalous behaviors, including Task Failure, Process Inefficiency, and Unwarranted Continuation.

---

[Bridging the Indoor-Outdoor Gap: Vision-Centric Instruction-Guided Embodied Navigation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06427)

- BridgeNav: introduces out-to-in prior-free instruction-driven embodied navigation, utilizing a vision-centric framework with a Multimodal LLM (vision-language understanding), Cross-Attention Modules (token interaction), Latent Intention Inference Module (salient region identification), Optical Flow-Guided Dynamic Perception Module (trajectory-visual change mapping), Text Encoder (language embedding), Vision Encoder (image encoding), and Decoder (trajectory prediction).
- The framework leverages image-based prompts and dynamic attention guided by a latent intention module to seamlessly transition navigation from coarse-grained outdoor scenes to fine-grained building entrances.
- The authors introduce the BridgeNavDataset, the first open-source dataset for this task, comprising 55k high-quality outdoor navigation trajectory-instruction pairs generated via trajectory-conditioned video synthesis.

---

[Near-Optimal Regret for Distributed Adversarial Bandits: A Black-Box Approach](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06404)

- BBR-DF (Black-Box Reduction to Delayed Feedback): introduces a block-based approach that decouples learning from communication via accelerated gossip to achieve near-optimal regret bounds for distributed adversarial K-armed bandits, utilizing Agents, a Communication Network, a Gossip Protocol, a Block-based Approach, a Delayed Bandit Algorithm, a Base OLO Algorithm, an Exploration Parameter, a Loss Estimator, and a Global Average Loss Estimate.
- The approach achieves a minimax regret rate of $\tilde{O}(\sqrt{(\rho^{-1/2} + K/N)T})$, significantly improving upon prior bounds, where $\rho$ is the spectral gap of the communication matrix, $K$ is the number of actions, $N$ is the number of agents, and $T$ is the horizon.
- The framework is extended to distributed adversarial linear bandits, achieving a regret bound of $\tilde{O}(\sqrt{(\rho^{-1/2} + d/N)dT})$ with $O(d)$ communication cost per agent per round via a volumetric spanner.

---

[D-ripALM: A Tuning-friendly Decentralized Relative-Type Inexact Proximal Augmented Lagrangian Method](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06398)

- D-ripALM (Decentralized relative-type inexact proximal Augmented Lagrangian Method): introduces a double-loop distributed optimization framework for consensus convex optimization over multi-agent networks, utilizing a relative-type error criterion to adaptively coordinate inner and outer iterations.
- The relative-type error criterion enhances numerical robustness and provides a tuning-friendly algorithmic framework by eliminating the need to pre-specify a summable absolute tolerance sequence.
- The double-loop structure allows for flexible, subsolver-agnostic implementation, enabling efficient treatment of both smooth and nonsmooth convex objectives without strong convexity assumptions.

---

[InterFlow: Designing Unobtrusive AI to Empower Interviewers in Semi-Structured Interviews](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06396)

- InterFlow: introduces an AI-powered visual scaffold for semi-structured interviews, featuring an Interactive Script (Dynamic Interview Structure), Visual Timer (Progress/Conversational Balance), and Mixed-initiative Information Capture (Manual/AI-assisted Note-taking).
- The system dynamically adapts the interview script to the ongoing conversation and facilitates real-time data sensemaking by reducing cognitive load for non-expert interviewers.
- The Co-interview Agent proactively surfaces potential follow-up points and inconsistencies using LLMs, designed to be unobtrusive and preserve interviewer agency.

[POINTS-GUI-G: GUI-Grounding Journey](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06391)

- POINTS-GUI-G: introduces a state-of-the-art GUI grounding model built upon the POINTS-1.5 architecture and Qwen3-8B backbone, enhanced by refined data engineering, improved training strategies, and reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards.
- The approach unfreezes the vision encoder and employs resolution optimization strategies to enhance perceptual accuracy for high-resolution GUI benchmarks.
- Reinforcement Learning is stabilized using Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) and curriculum learning, leveraging precise binary rewards derived from bounding box intersection for grounding tasks.

---

[Revisiting Salient Object Detection from an Observer-Centric Perspective](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06369)

- OC-SODAgent: introduces an agentic baseline for Observer-Centric Salient Object Detection (OC-SOD) that uses an MLLM (Reasoning Core/Reflection Agent), SAMv2 (Segmentation Model), and a Render Component (Visual Input Synthesizer) to perform saliency prediction.
- The framework operates in two stages: an Initial Prediction Stage followed by an iterative Perceive-Reflect-Adjust Cycle, mimicking human-like reasoning and refinement.
- OC-SOD reformulates Salient Object Detection (SOD) as a conditional generation problem guided by observer-specific factors, including free-viewing, preference-driven, and intent-driven modes, supported by the new OC-SODBench dataset.

---

[Quenching Speculation in Quantum Markets via Entangled Neural Traders](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06367)

- Quantum Stock Market Framework (QSMF): introduces a prototype quantum stock market where reinforcement learning (RL) agents trade a commodity using quantum-correlated qubit-encoded valuations to stabilize prices.
- The framework utilizes a variational quantum circuit to entangle the raw valuations of the RL agents, transforming the strategic landscape and eliminating the pathological classical bust-type Nash equilibrium.
- Simulations demonstrate that quantum entanglement mitigates runaway devaluation, resulting in higher average net worth for traders compared to analogous classical markets.

---

[Towards Adaptive Environment Generation for Training Embodied Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06366)

- Closed-Loop Environment Generation: introduces a proof-of-concept system for adaptively generating training environments by employing a controllable environment representation, extracting fine-grained performance feedback using an LLM Analysis Model ($F$), and implementing a closed-loop adaptation mechanism via an LLM Environment Generator ($G$).
- The framework creates an adaptive curriculum where training environments ($e_{t+1}$) grow progressively more challenging based on the agent's current capabilities and specific weaknesses identified in its trajectory analysis ($a_t$).
- The system utilizes LLMs for both trajectory analysis and environment modification, constrained by a Collision-aware Placement Module to ensure physical plausibility and task solvability in the generated scenes.

---

[Envy-Free Allocation of Indivisible Goods via Noisy Queries](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06361)

- TBA-EFA: introduces the problem of envy-free allocation of indivisible goods between two agents using noisy queries, establishing optimal query complexity bounds.
- The optimal number of queries $q$ required to find an envy-free allocation scales as $\tilde{\Theta}(m^{2.5}/\Delta^2)$, where $m$ is the number of items and $\Delta$ is the optimal negative envy gap.
- The upper bound algorithm utilizes a non-adaptive querying strategy and a polynomial-time item-by-item thresholding rule under an additive Gaussian noise model.

---

[Nipping the Drift in the Bud: Retrospective Rectification for Robust Vision-Language Navigation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06356)

- BudVLN: introduces a unified online training framework that uses an Adaptive Mutual Exclusion Strategy to dynamically route training between optimality-seeking exploration (GRPO) and failure prevention (Retrospective Rectification/SFT).
- The framework addresses Instruction-State Misalignment inherent in DAgger by employing Retrospective Rectification, which re-anchors the agent to valid historical states to synthesize semantically consistent, forward-looking corrective trajectories using a geodesic oracle.
- BudVLN achieves state-of-the-art performance in Vision-Language Navigation benchmarks (R2R-CE and RxR-CE) while requiring only about 25% of the training cost compared to standard DAgger pipelines.

---

[Trifuse: Enhancing Attention-Based GUI Grounding via Multimodal Fusion](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06351)

- Trifuse: introduces an attention-based GUI grounding framework that fuses MLLM attention, OCR-based textual cues, and icon caption-based visual semantics using a Consensus-SinglePeak (CS) fusion strategy.
- The framework employs a Modality Extraction Module to derive complementary heatmaps, followed by the CS Fusion Module to balance cross-modal agreement and modality-specific discriminative peaks.
- Trifuse achieves strong grounding performance without task-specific fine-tuning by utilizing a two-stage localization strategy to refine coarse predictions from the fused heatmap.

---

[ZERO-TRUST RUNTIME VERIFICATION FOR AGENTIC PAYMENT PROTOCOLS: MITIGATING REPLAY AND CONTEXT-BINDING FAILURES IN AP2](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06345)

- ZTRV: introduces a zero-trust runtime verification framework for Agent Payments Protocol (AP2) mandates, enforcing context-aware binding and consume-once semantics using dynamically generated nonces.
- The framework mitigates replay and context-redirect attacks in highly concurrent agent runtimes by ensuring authorization decisions are evaluated at execution time rather than relying on static issuance properties.
- Evaluation shows ZTRV achieves a 100% interception rate against tested attacks while maintaining stable, low verification latency (approx. 3.8 ms at 10,000 transactions per second).

---

[Ornstein-Uhlenbeck information particle: A new candidate of active agent](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06340)

- OUIP (Ornstein-Uhlenbeck Information Particle): introduces an active agent model where an underdamped Brownian particle acquires self-propulsion via an information engine using OU bath feedback control, adjusting the persistence time based on measured velocity.
- The OUIP exhibits two distinct dynamical patterns: a slow-speed diffusion mode and a high-speed traveling mode, which can be flexibly tuned by adjusting the particle's inertial effect (reduced mass $M$).
- By tuning the perturbation strength ($\tilde{A}$) of the OU bath, the OUIP can achieve a wide range of net average velocities, demonstrating rich and non-trivial motion behavior compared to standard self-propelled particles (SPP).

[Identifying Adversary Tactics and Techniques in Malware Binaries with an LLM Agent](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06325)

- TTPDetect: introduces the first LLM agent for recognizing Tactics, Techniques, and Procedures (TTPs) in stripped malware binaries, utilizing a Renaming Agent, hybrid Dense/Neural Retrieval, and an Analyzing Agent with a Context Explorer and TTP-Specific Reasoning Guideline.
- The approach scales to large binaries by employing a hybrid retrieval strategy combining dense retrieval and LLM-based neural retrieval to efficiently narrow the vast space of candidate function–TTP pairs.
- The function-level analysis agent mitigates partial observability via incremental context retrieval and achieves inference-time alignment using pre-synthesized TTP-Specific Reasoning Guidelines, achieving 93.25% precision and 93.81% recall on function-level TTP recognition.

[Trustworthy AI Software Engineers](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06310)

- Trustworthy AI Software Engineer: introduces a working definition for an AI agent to qualify as an AI software engineer, emphasizing capabilities beyond coding, such as planning, multi-step execution, context reasoning, and collaboration within human-AI SE teams.
- The paper distinguishes trust (human decision) from trustworthiness (system property) and identifies core dimensions spanning technical quality, transparency, epistemic humility, and societal/ethical alignment necessary for justified reliance.
- This vision paper advocates for an ethics-by-design approach and continuous, context-sensitive assessment to enable appropriate trust in future human-AI SE systems.

[Lost in Speech: Benchmarking, Evaluation, and Parsing of Spoken Code-Switching Beyond Standard UD Assumptions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06307)

- DECAP (DECoupled Agentic Parser): introduces a modular, instruction-grounded framework for parsing spoken code-switching (CSW) language by isolating spoken-phenomena handling from core syntactic analysis using specialized LLM agents.
- The DECAP framework sequentially processes input through four specialized LLM agents: the Spoken-Phenomena Handler, the Language-Specific Resolver, the Core UD Structure Assigner, and the Verifier and Ranker.
- The research also introduces SpokeBench, a gold benchmark for spoken CSW, and FLEX-UD, an ambiguity-aware evaluation metric that tolerates linguistically defensible variation while penalizing catastrophic structural errors.

---

[Do LLMs Act Like Rational Agents? Measuring Belief Coherence in Probabilistic Decision Making](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06286)

- BCF: introduces a decision-theoretic framework to test whether LLM-elicited probabilities are consistent with observed actions, using Random Utility Model (RUM) or Prospect-Theoretic Random Utility Model (PT-RUM) models and statistical tests, applied to medical diagnosis tasks.
- The framework tests belief coherence by deriving falsifiable constraints that link reported beliefs ($P_E(\theta|x)$) to choices ($a$), quantifying the degree of deviation from ideal Bayesian utility maximization.
- Empirical evaluation across multiple LLMs and medical datasets finds that elicited beliefs and actions are provably not fully consistent with rational decision making, though the degree of deviation is often mild.

---

[SAGE: Benchmarking and Improving Retrieval for Deep Research Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05975)

- SAGE: introduces a benchmark for reasoning-intensive scientific literature retrieval and proposes a corpus-level test-time scaling framework to improve retrieval performance for deep research agents.
- The paper evaluates six deep research agents on SAGE, finding that existing agents generate keyword-oriented sub-queries, causing LLM-based retrievers to underperform BM25 by approximately 30%.
- The corpus-level test-time scaling framework uses an LLM to augment documents with metadata and keywords, yielding up to 8% performance gains on short-form questions.

#### 5th February 2026

[On Randomized Algorithms in Online Strategic Classification](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06257)

- ROSC Algorithms: introduces refined upper and lower bounds for online strategic classification in both realizable and agnostic settings using a Learner (Selects hypothesis distribution), Adversary (Selects strategic agent), Randomization Mechanism (Biased coin flip), Exploration Strategy (All-positive classifier), Expert Strategy (Samples consistent hypothesis), and FTRL Framework (Log-barrier regularization).
- The paper provides the first randomized algorithm (Uniform-Mix/Expert-Mix) that improves the known deterministic upper bound for the realizable setting when the time horizon $T$ is small.
- For the agnostic setting, the approach establishes an optimal regret upper bound among proper learners using a Follow-the-Regularized-Leader (FTRL) framework with a log-barrier regularizer.

---

[RuleSmith: Multi-Agent LLMs for Automated Game Balancing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06232)

- RuleSmith: introduces a framework for automated game balancing by integrating a Bayesian Optimization Engine, an LLM Self-Play Evaluator, and the CivMini Game Engine, which optimizes asymmetric game rule parameters using LLM agents performing zero-shot self-play.
- The framework employs Bayesian optimization over a continuous rule space, coupled with acquisition-based adaptive sampling, to efficiently search for balanced configurations that minimize win-rate disparities.
- LLM agents interpret natural-language rulebooks and game states to generate actions, enabling the evaluation of balance metrics and yielding interpretable rule adjustments.

---

[Dynamic Quantum Optimal Communication Topology Design for Consensus Control in Linear Multi-Agent Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06215)

- Dynamic Quantum Optimal Communication Topology Design Framework: introduces a quantum framework for online communication topology design in consensus-based linear MASs by decomposing the MIQP into a Classical Convex Subproblem, a Pure Binary Subproblem, and an Auxiliary Update, where the binary core is solved using QITE.
- The approach uses a three-block ADMM splitting to handle the mixed-integer quadratic program (MIQP), ensuring graph connectivity via a flow-based formulation and enforcing degree constraints.
- The Pure Binary Subproblem is mapped to a QUBO Hamiltonian, which is approximately solved by the fully quantum QITE algorithm to generate time-varying, connected, degree-bounded communication topologies for consensus control.

---

[Threshold Resource Redistribution in Spatially-Structured Kinship Networks](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06200)

- TRRM: introduces a model for threshold-based resource redistribution in a spatially-explicit population, characterizing the relationship between kinship network structure, local interactions, and population persistence.
- The model analyzes agent survival based on stochastic resource input and cooperative transfers, where the transfer fraction depends on relatedness (generational distance) and spatial distance.
- Redistribution enables population survival at lower resource densities but leads to increased network heterogeneity, locally centralized clusters, and preferential survival of highly-connected agents (hubs).

---

[Active Localization of Unstable Systems with Coarse Information](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06191)

- ACTIVELOCALIZE: introduces an active localization algorithm for unstable linear systems under coarse, single-bit sensing, integrating a set-based estimator (ESTIMATE) with a control strategy (RCS) derived from Spherical Voronoi Partitions (SVP).
- The approach guarantees exponential contraction of the initial-state uncertainty by leveraging system instability to aid estimation and employing a recovery control strategy to ensure the agent remains within the sensing region.
- The set-based estimator refines estimates of the initial state and landmark location using ellipsoid intersections and reachable set computations based on persistent positive measurements.

---

[M3: High-fidelity Text-to-Image Generation via Multi-Modal, Multi-Agent and Multi-Round Visual Reasoning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06166)

- M3 (Multi-Modal, Multi-Agent, Multi-Round): introduces a training-free, closed-loop agentic framework that systematically refines text-to-image generation outputs through iterative visual reasoning.
- The core architecture employs a multi-round optimization process where a Planner creates a checklist, and Checker, Refiner, Editor, and Verifier agents progressively correct alignment failures.
- M3 achieves state-of-the-art performance on compositional benchmarks by surgically correcting errors in spatial relationships, attribute binding, and object counting without costly retraining.

---

[Flow Matching for Offline Reinforcement Learning with Discrete Actions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06138)

- QDFM (Q-weighted discrete flow matching): introduces a generative policy optimization framework for offline RL that replaces continuous probability flows with a Continuous-Time Markov Chain (CTMC) over discrete actions.
- The method learns a transition-rate model via discrete flow matching, enabling efficient action generation for varying preferences without retraining, guided by value-based endpoint reweighting.
- QDFM is theoretically grounded, showing that optimizing the Q-weighted conditional objective recovers the KL-regularized optimal policy in discrete action spaces.

---

[Hear You in Silence: Designing for Active Listening in Human Interaction with Conversational Agents Using Context-Aware Pacing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06134)

- Context-Aware Pacing CA: introduces a conversational agent that dynamically adjusts response timing using five context-aware pacing strategies (Reflective Silence, Facilitative Silence, Empathic Silence, Holding Space, Immediate Response) to simulate active listening.
- The system architecture includes a Context Analysis Module for strategy selection, a Response Generation Module for paced output, and a Conversational Memory Module for context coherence, leveraging the GPT-4o LLM.
- A user study demonstrated that context-aware pacing significantly enhanced perceived human-likeness, smoothness, interactivity, and affective trust, leading to deeper user self-disclosure and engagement compared to static pacing.

---

[DyTopo: Dynamic Topology Routing for Multi-Agent Reasoning via Semantic Matching](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06039)

- DyTopo: introduces a manager-guided multi-agent framework that dynamically reconstructs a sparse directed communication graph at each round using semantic matching between agents' natural-language Query (need) and Key (offer) descriptors.
- The framework utilizes a Semantic Matching Engine to embed descriptors and quantify relevance, routing private messages only along activated links defined by a hard threshold, thereby decoupling message generation from information routing.
- DyTopo consistently improves performance over fixed and random topology baselines across code generation and mathematical reasoning tasks, yielding an interpretable coordination trace via evolving communication graphs.

---

[CommCP: Efficient Multi-Agent Coordination via LLM-Based Communication with Conformal Prediction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06038)

- CommCP (Efficient Multi-Agent Coordination via LLM-Based Communication with Conformal Prediction): introduces a novel LLM-based decentralized communication framework for Multi-Agent Multi-Task Embodied Question Answering (MM-EQA), featuring perception, communication, planning, and confidence check modules.
- The framework leverages Conformal Prediction (CP) to calibrate LLM-generated messages, ensuring that agents only communicate information they confidently deem relevant to partner tasks, thereby enhancing communication reliability.
- CommCP significantly enhances task success rate and exploration efficiency in photo-realistic household scenarios by enabling strategic information exchange and coordinated exploration via a Semantic Value Map.

---

[V-Retrver: Evidence-Driven Agentic Reasoning for Universal Multimodal Retrieval](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06034)

- V-Retrver: introduces an evidence-driven retrieval framework that reformulates universal multimodal retrieval as an agentic reasoning process grounded in visual inspection, utilizing an Embedding Model, a Reasoning Agent, Visual Tools, MIER, and a Curriculum-Based Training Strategy.
- The framework employs a coarse-to-fine pipeline where the Reasoning Agent performs Multimodal Interleaved Evidence Reasoning (MIER), alternating between hypothesis generation and targeted visual verification via external visual tools (SELECT-IMAGE and ZOOM-IN).
- Training V-Retrver uses a curriculum strategy consisting of Supervised Fine-Tuning (SFT), Rejection Sampling Fine-Tuning (RSFT), and Evidence-Aligned Policy Optimization (EAPO) to ensure reasoning quality and efficient visual tool usage.

---

[PhysicsAgentABM: Physics-Guided Generative Agent-Based Modeling](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06030)

- PhysicsAgentABM: introduces a hierarchical neuro-symbolic framework that shifts generative Agent-Based Modeling (ABM) inference from individual agents to adaptive agent clusters, utilizing symbolic and neural pathways fused with uncertainty-aware epistemic fusion.
- The framework employs ANCHOR, an LLM-agent-driven multi-stage clustering mechanism, to organize agents into behaviorally coherent clusters based on cross-contextual similarity and interaction structure, significantly reducing LLM calls.
- Cluster-level inference defines population-consistent transition priors, which individual agents then stochastically realize under local constraints, decoupling population dynamics from entity-level variability for scalable simulation.

---

[Curiosity is Knowledge: Self-Consistent Learning and No-Regret Optimization with Active Inference](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06029)

- Pragmatic Curiosity (Active Inference): establishes the first theoretical guarantee that a single requirement—sufficient curiosity—simultaneously ensures self-consistent learning (posterior consistency) and no-regret optimization (bounded cumulative regret) for EFE-minimizing agents.
- The framework utilizes an acquisition rule that maximizes the trade-off between the epistemic term (information gain) and the pragmatic term (expected regret), scaled by the curiosity coefficient $\beta_t$.
- The research translates these theoretical bounds into practical design guidelines, demonstrating that sufficient curiosity is the critical mechanism coupling belief updating and decision-making in hybrid learning-optimization problems.

---

[Learning Query-Aware Budget-Tier Routing for Runtime Agent Memory](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06025)

- BudgetMem: introduces a runtime agent memory framework enabling explicit performance-cost control for on-demand memory extraction using a modular pipeline and budget-tiered modules.
- The framework employs a shared lightweight router trained via reinforcement learning (PPO) to dynamically select LOW/MID/HIGH budget tiers for each module based on the query and intermediate states.
- Budget tiers are realized through three complementary strategies: implementation (varying module complexity), reasoning (varying inference behavior), and capacity (varying model size/LLM backbone).

---

[AgenticPay: A Multi-Agent LLM Negotiation System for Buyer-Seller Transactions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06008)

- AgenticPay: introduces a benchmark and simulation framework for multi-agent buyer-seller negotiation, including Agents (LLM-based policies), Environment (Negotiation protocol/scenarios), Task (Market structure/complexity), Metrics (Evaluation/scoring), Conversation History (Dialogue memory), and Public/Private Information (Context/valuations), where agents negotiate through multi-round linguistic dialogue to reach economic agreements.
- The framework formalizes negotiation as a language game spanning 111 tasks from bilateral bargaining to full many-to-many markets, modeling private constraints and product-dependent valuations.
- Evaluation metrics capture deal feasibility, efficiency, and welfare, revealing that proprietary LLMs significantly outperform open-weight models, which struggle with long-horizon strategic reasoning and convergence.

---

[From Human-Human Collaboration to Human-Agent Collaboration: A Vision, Design Philosophy, and an Empirical Framework for Achieving Successful Partnerships Between Humans and LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05987)

- HACF: introduces a novel research agenda by proposing the "agent as a remote collaborator" analogy to design LLM agents as genuine partners, utilizing Human (user partner), Interface (interaction medium), LLM Agent (intelligent collaborator), Remote Collaborator Analogy (design philosophy), and CSCW Theories (foundational concepts).
- The framework shifts the paradigm from LLMs acting as passive tools to proactive collaborators capable of mixed-initiative interaction, reasoning, and planning.
- This vision grounds human-agent collaboration in decades of research on distributed teamwork, focusing on concepts like common ground, workspace awareness, and articulation work.

---

[Learning to Share: Selective Memory for Efficient Parallel Agentic Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05965)

- LTS (Learning to Share): introduces a learned shared-memory mechanism for parallel agentic systems that enables selective cross-team information reuse to reduce redundant computation.
- The system utilizes a Global Shared Memory Bank accessible to all teams and a lightweight Memory Controller trained via stepwise reinforcement learning with usage-aware reward shaping.
- LTS significantly reduces overall wall-clock runtime and improves task performance compared to memory-free parallel baselines on GAIA and AssistantBench benchmarks.

---

[Location-Aware Dispersion on Anonymous Graphs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05948)

- LOCATION-AWARE DISPERSION: introduces a generalization of the DISPERSION problem incorporating color constraints, solved using deterministic algorithms based on a Depth-First Search (DFS) strategy, group/supernode formation, and a three-phase approach for arbitrary graphs.
- The algorithms operate in synchronous Communicate-Compute-Move (CCM) cycles, minimizing time and memory requirements for mobile robots operating on anonymous, port-labeled, memory-less graphs.
- The research establishes algorithmic feasibility and fundamental limitations for LAD, providing complexity bounds for various initial configurations and robot knowledge assumptions regarding $n$ (nodes) and $k$ (robots).

---

[AgenticTagger: Structured Item Representation for Recommendation with LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05945)

- AgenticTagger: introduces a multi-LLM agent framework for generating structured, hierarchical, low-cardinality natural language descriptor features for items, utilizing Architect- and Annotator-LLMs for vocabulary refinement and assignment.
- The framework operates in two core stages: vocabulary building, which constructs an interpretable, hierarchical descriptor taxonomy, and vocabulary assignment, which constrains LLMs to assign in-vocabulary descriptors to items in parallel.
- AgenticTagger features a multi-agent reflection mechanism where a stronger Architect LLM iteratively refines the vocabulary based on parallelized error feedback from multiple Annotator LLMs to ensure broad item coverage.

[QUANTUM REINFORCEMENT LEARNING WITH TRANSFORMERS FOR THE CAPACITATED VEHICLE ROUTING PROBLEM](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05920)

- Quantum Reinforcement Learning with Transformers (QRL-T): introduces a quantum Advantage Actor-Critic (A2C) framework integrating transformer architectures (CPN, HQP, FQP) to solve the dynamic multi-vehicle Capacitated Vehicle Routing Problem (CVRP).
- The approach compares classical, hybrid, and fully quantum Pointer Networks, utilizing self- and cross-attention mechanisms to capture relationships between vehicles, clients, and the depot.
- Quantum-enhanced models, particularly the Hybrid Quantum Pointer Network (HQP), outperform the classical baseline in routing distance, route overlap, and spatial coherence metrics.

---

[CONTEXTBENCH: A Benchmark for Context Retrieval in Coding Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05892)

- CONTEXTBENCH: introduces a process-oriented benchmark for context retrieval in LLM coding agents, featuring human-annotated Gold Contexts and an Automated Evaluation Framework that tracks agent trajectories and measures context recall, precision, and F1 at file, block, and line granularities.
- The benchmark comprises 1,136 issue resolution tasks from 66 repositories across eight programming languages, annotated with over 522,000 lines of human-verified gold contexts.
- Evaluation results show that sophisticated agent scaffolding provides marginal gains in context retrieval, LLMs consistently favor recall over precision, and significant gaps exist between retrieved and utilized context.

---

[Metric Hedonic Games on the Line](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05888)

- Metric Hedonic Games (MHG): introduces a novel succinct variant of hedonic games where agents' costs are derived from metric distances (type differences) within their coalition, utilizing AVERAGE, MAXIMUM, and CUTOFF cost functions.
- The research investigates the existence, structural properties (e.g., sorted coalition structures), and quality (Price of Anarchy and Price of Stability) of stable coalition structures under JUMP and SWAP stability concepts.
- The study finds that stable coalition structures always exist across all cost functions and stability concepts, but their properties and quality (PoA/PoS) vary widely, often resulting in unbounded PoA.

---

[Agent2Agent Threats in Safety-Critical LLM Assistants: A Human-Centric Taxonomy](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05877)

- AGENTHELLM (Agent Hazard Exploration for LLM Assistants): introduces a threat modeling framework for safety-critical LLM assistants, formally separating assets (WHAT) using a human-centric taxonomy from attack paths (HOW) using a formal graph model.
- The framework models agentic systems using Actor nodes (entities with agency) and Datasource nodes (passive stores) connected by interaction primitives (read, write, communicate, respond).
- The model distinguishes between Poison Paths (malicious data propagation) and Trigger Paths (activation actions), capturing the recursive "attack within attack" structure common in LLM vulnerabilities.

[DuoDrama: Supporting Screenplay Refinement Through LLM-Assisted Human Reflection](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05854)

- DuoDrama (Experience-Grounded Feedback Generation Workflow for Human Reflection, ExReflect): introduces a multi-agent LLM system that supports screenplay refinement by coordinating internal character experience and external actor evaluation through sequential role-playing.
- The ExReflect workflow utilizes a single agent to first adopt an experience role to generate personal inner thoughts, and then shift to an evaluation role to generate contextually aligned feedback questions.
- The system employs a dual-memory module and a self-verification mechanism to ensure feedback is grounded in enacted experience and aligned with narrative context and quality criteria.

[DARWIN: Dynamic Agentically Rewriting Self-Improving Network](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05848)

- DARWIN (Dynamic Agentically Rewriting Self-Improving Network): introduces an evolutionary GPT framework utilizing a genetic algorithm-like optimization structure where GPT Agents modify the training code of one another in a mutation-like manner, with all components operating within isolated containers.
- The architecture is composed of four modules: a Central Controller, a Model Cloning/Training/Selection Module, an LLM Mutation Engine, and a Memory/Communication Module, which manage the iterative training and self-improvement process.
- The system utilizes Persistent Memory (JSON logs) to track modification history and a Bidirectional HITL Interface to facilitate human guidance and agent requests for resources or structural changes, supplementing the LLM-mediated code mutation.

---

[ODYSSEYARENA: Benchmarking Large Language Models For Long-Horizon, Active and Inductive Interactions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05843)

- ODYSSEYARENA: introduces a benchmarking suite for LLMs centered on long-horizon, active, and inductive interactions, featuring an LLM Agent, Working Memory, and four environments: Turn On Lights (Discrete symbolic rules), AI Trading (Continuous stochastic dynamics), Energy Dispatch (Periodic temporal patterns), and Repo System (Relational graph structures).
- The framework shifts agent evaluation from the traditional deductive paradigm, which relies on explicit rules, to an inductive mode, requiring agents to autonomously discover latent transition laws through strategic interaction and exploration.
- Evaluation across 15+ LLMs reveals a fundamental inductive bottleneck, where even frontier models struggle significantly in scenarios demanding autonomous discovery of hidden world dynamics over extended horizons.

---

[Reinforcement World Model Learning for LLM-based Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05842)

- RWML (Reinforcement World Model Learning): introduces a scalable, self-supervised method to train LLM-based agents as action-conditioned world models by aligning simulated next states with observed environment states using a sim-to-real gap reward.
- The method utilizes an embedding model to measure semantic consistency between predicted and real next states, providing a robust training signal less susceptible to reward hacking than LLM-as-a-judge approaches.
- RWML significantly improves base model performance on long-horizon benchmarks (ALFWorld and $\tau^2$ Bench) and, when combined with task-success reward RL, outperforms direct task-success reward RL while matching expert-data training performance.

---

[Bandit Social Learning with Exploration Episodes](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05835)

- EpiBSL (Episodic Bandit Social Learning): introduces a stylized social learning dynamics model where self-interested agents control multi-round episodes ($m \geq 2$) in a multi-armed bandit setting, aiming to maximize their Bayesian-expected utility.
- The research demonstrates that aggregate exploration fails in EpiBSL, showing that learning failures are typical for any fixed episode length $m$, leading to linearly scaling Bayesian regret over time.
- The model incorporates a common Bayesian prior, exploration costs, and a generic aggregation function $f$ (e.g., sum, max, min) to calculate per-episode scores from observed rewards, analyzing the exploration-exploitation tradeoff.

---

[UI-Mem: Self-Evolving Experience Memory for Online Reinforcement Learning in Mobile GUI Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05832)

- UI-Mem: introduces a novel framework enhancing GUI online RL with a Hierarchical Experience Memory that stores structured knowledge (workflows, subtask skills, failure patterns) as parameterized templates.
- The framework utilizes Stratified Group Sampling during Memory-Guided Exploration to inject varying levels of guidance, ensuring outcome diversity essential for effective Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO).
- A Self-Evolving Loop continuously abstracts successful plans and failure diagnoses from new trajectories, dynamically updating the memory pool to co-evolve with the agent's policy and enable cross-task transfer.

[Weaver: End-to-End Agentic System Training for Video Interleaved Reasoning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05829)

- Weaver: introduces an end-to-end trainable multimodal reasoning agentic system, including a policy model (VLM for stepwise reasoning), a tool library (specialized visual perception tools), and a history state (accumulated textual/visual information), enabling interleaved visual-text reasoning for complex video tasks.
- The system employs a two-stage training strategy: supervised fine-tuning for basic tool invocation followed by tool-augmented reinforcement learning for autonomous exploration and optimization of tool compositions using trajectory-free data.
- Weaver generates multimodal reasoning trajectories by dynamically invoking perception tools to progressively acquire crucial spatio-temporal visual evidence, mitigating hallucination and enhancing performance on long video benchmarks.

[Sparse Video Generation Propels Real-World Beyond-the-View Vision-Language Navigation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05827)

- SparseVideoNav: introduces a novel paradigm for Beyond-the-View Navigation (BVN) by leveraging a Video Generation Model (VGM) to produce Sparse Future Video Latents for long-horizon foresight, overcoming short-sightedness in LLM baselines.
- The system employs a structured four-stage training pipeline, including History Injection and Diffusion Distillation, to achieve sub-second trajectory inference guided by a 20-second sparse future horizon, resulting in a 27x speed-up over unoptimized counterparts.
- The architecture integrates a VGM backbone, a History Compression Module (Q-Former and Video-Former), and a Diffusion Transformer (DiT) action head to map current and historical observations and language instructions to continuous actions for real-world deployment.

[Whispers of the Butterfly: A Research-through-Design Exploration of In-Situ Conversational AI Guidance in Large-Scale Outdoor MR Exhibitions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05826)

- Dream-Butterfly: introduces an in-situ conversational AI docent embodied as a small non-human companion for large-scale outdoor Mixed Reality (MR) art exhibitions, utilizing a Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) backend grounded in exhibition materials.
- The research uses a Research-through-Design approach and an in-the-wild comparative study (N=24) contrasting an AI-first guiding configuration with a human-led tour, while maintaining human staff for safety oversight in both.
- Findings indicate that configuring the AI guide as the primary, pull-based interpretation channel improves explanation access and hedonic quality without increasing perceived workload, shifting pacing and inquiry responsibility to the visitor.

[TKG-Thinker: Towards Dynamic Reasoning over Temporal Knowledge Graphs via Agentic Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05818)

- TKG-Thinker: introduces a novel LLM Agent (autonomous planning, adaptive retrieval) that performs dynamic multi-turn temporal reasoning over Temporal Knowledge Graphs (TKGs) using a dual-training strategy: Supervised Fine-Tuning and Online Reinforcement Learning.
- The agent utilizes a ReAct-style think-action-observation loop and specialized Temporal Tools (search_time, search_before, etc.) to ensure verified, temporally grounded evidence retrieval, mitigating reasoning hallucinations.
- The RL stage employs a multi-objective reward mechanism incorporating outcome, format, and retrieval rewards to optimize reasoning policies under complex temporal constraints.

---

[BIFROST: Steering STRATEGIC TRAJECTORIES TO BRIDGE CONTEXTUAL GAPS FOR SELF-IMPROVING AGENTS](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05810)

- Bifrost (Bridge contextual gap FoR improvised trajectory STeering): introduces a training-free framework that leverages context differences to precisely guide the adaptation of previously solved trajectories toward a target task, mitigating misalignment caused by context shifts.
- The method operates at the representation level by calculating a Contextual Direction Vector from agent hidden states, ensuring trajectory transformation accurately aligns with the target context in a shared space.
- Bifrost significantly enhances cross-context generalization for self-improving agents across diverse benchmarks, including math reasoning and code generation, by exploiting the context-trajectory correlation.

[Privacy-Preserving Dynamic Average Consensus by Masking Reference Signals](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05803)

- PP-DAC: introduces a privacy-preserving dynamic average consensus algorithm that masks agents' reference signals using random offsets exchanged over encrypted channels.
- The approach ensures that the average of the masked reference signals remains equal to the average of the true reference signals, preserving tracking accuracy.
- The proposed algorithm matches the convergence rate of conventional DAC while providing privacy guarantees against external eavesdroppers and internal honest-but-curious agents.

---

[ROCQSMITH: CAN AUTOMATIC OPTIMIZATION FORGE BETTER PROOF AGENTS?](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05762)

- ROCQSMITH: evaluates automatic agent optimization methods on a simplified Rocq proof agent core, implemented using the DSPy framework and GPT-4.1 LLM, for generating proofs in the Rocq Interactive Theorem Prover environment.
- The study compares prompt-centric optimizers (BootstrapFewShot, MIPROv2, SIMBA, GEPA), context-centric optimizers (ACE, ReasoningBank), and control flow optimizers (ADAS) against a human-engineered state-of-the-art agent.
- Results indicate that while several optimizers yield measurable improvements, simple few-shot bootstrapping is the most consistently effective, though none match the performance of the carefully engineered human baseline.

---

[Learning to Inject: Automated Prompt Injection via Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05746)

- AutoInject: introduces a reinforcement learning framework that generates universal, transferable adversarial suffixes by jointly optimizing for attack success and utility preservation using a composite reward signal derived from security, utility, and comparison-based feedback.
- The framework employs Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) to train an Attack Policy (Qwen2.5-1.5B) using dense intermediate rewards provided by a Feedback Model (GPT-4o-mini) that compares candidate suffixes against a reference suffix.
- AutoInject establishes a stronger baseline for automated prompt injection research by successfully compromising frontier LLM systems on the AgentDojo benchmark while maintaining high utility on benign tasks.

[A Dual-Loop Agent Framework for Automated Vulnerability Reproduction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05721)

- CVE2POC: introduces a dual-loop agent framework for automated vulnerability reproduction, utilizing Strategic Planner (vulnerability analysis, attack planning), Tactical Executor (PoC generation, progressive verification), and Adaptive Refiner (failure diagnosis, feedback routing) to generate executable Proof-of-Concept (PoC) exploits from CVE descriptions.
- The dual-loop architecture separates strategic planning from tactical execution, employing a Tactical Loop for code refinement and a Strategic Loop for fundamental strategy replanning to avoid ineffective debugging loops.
- The framework achieves high efficiency and accuracy by using a progressive multi-layer Oracle Engine for verification and an IndexedRewardStore for sparse experience retrieval, significantly reducing token consumption compared to baselines.

---

[Almost Asymptotically Optimal Active Clustering Through Pairwise Observations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05690)

- A³CNP (Almost Asymptotically Optimal Active Clustering with Noisy Pairwise Observations): introduces a principled framework for active clustering using noisy pairwise observations, deriving an instance-dependent lower bound on query complexity.
- The A³CNP algorithm achieves near-asymptotic optimality by combining statistically efficient sampling, guided by the optimal allocation solver $\lambda^*(\sigma; C_t)$, with a computationally tractable stopping rule $\tau_\delta$ based on the feasible test statistic $\tilde{Z}(t)$.
- The approach frames the clustering task as a pure-exploration bandit problem in the fixed-confidence regime, minimizing the expected number of queries required to identify the correct clustering with high probability.

[CROSS: A Continual Robotic Simulation Suite for Scalable Reinforcement Learning with High Task Diversity and Realistic Physics Simulation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04868)

- CROSS (Continual Robotic Simulation Suite): introduces a novel benchmark suite for Continual Reinforcement Learning (CRL) using realistic robotic simulations in Gazebo, featuring two distinct robotic platforms and high task diversity.
- The suite includes a two-wheeled differential-drive robot for line-following and object-pushing tasks, and a 7-d.o.f. robotic arm for high- and low-level reaching tasks, supporting both physics-based and faster kinematic simulations.
- CROSS provides a containerized setup (Apptainer) and leverages Gazebo-Transport for sim-to-real compatibility, enabling scalable and reproducible CRL research using standard RL algorithms like DQN and REINFORCE as baselines.

[El Agente Quntur: A research collaborator agent for quantum chemistry](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04850)

- EL AGENTE QUNTUR: introduces a hierarchical, multi-agent LLM system designed as a research collaborator for computational quantum chemistry, featuring a Computational Chemist agent, a Multi-agent Hierarchical Architecture, Procedural Memory, Long-term Memory, Agent-specific Memory, a Guided Deep Research Module, an Input File Service, a Geometry Generation Module, an Interact with OS and Files Agent, a Submission System, Domain Experts, and Tools (ORCA, XTB, RDKit, MinerU).
- QUNTUR supports the full range of calculations available in ORCA 6.0 and reasons over software documentation and scientific literature to plan, execute, adapt, and analyze in silico chemistry experiments.

[El Agente Estructural: An Artificially Intelligent Molecular Editor](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04849)

- ESTRUCTURAL: introduces a multimodal, natural-language-driven geometry-generation and manipulation agent for autonomous chemistry and molecular modeling, with all geometry operator agent (High-level planning/reasoning/orchestration), Vision-Language Model (Top-level agent/Multimodal reasoning), Structural Editing Tools (Atom/fragment/branch replacement), Structural Generation Tools (SMILES/Name-to-XYZ/Organometallic construction), Structural Analysis Tools (Visual inspection/Index identification/Symmetry/Fragment analysis), Geometric Operation Tools (Distance/Angle/Dihedral/Rotation/Constrained optimization), Python execution environment (Code execution/Custom analysis), and Image-pruning context management strategy (Visual token reduction/Context management) components, designed to mimic how human experts directly manipulate molecular systems in three dimensions.
- The agent operates directly on three-dimensional Cartesian coordinates using atomic index-centric geometry operations, enabling precise control over atomic or functional group replacements, connectivity, and stereochemistry without rebuilding core molecular frameworks.
- ESTRUCTURAL performs complex tasks like site-selective functionalization, stereochemically specific construction, and image-guided generation of transition states by composing specialized geometry-aware tools and multimodal reasoning.

[Group-Evolving Agents: Open-Ended Self-Improvement via Experience Sharing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04837)

- GEA (Group-Evolving Agents): introduces a new paradigm for open-ended self-improvement that treats a group of agents as the fundamental evolutionary unit, enabling explicit experience sharing and reuse within the group throughout evolution.
- The framework proceeds in two core stages: Parent Group Selection, which uses a Performance-Novelty criterion, and Open-ended Group Evolution, where agents jointly produce offspring by leveraging aggregated experience.
- GEA significantly outperforms tree-structured self-evolving methods on coding benchmarks by effectively consolidating exploratory diversity into sustained, long-term progress, and demonstrates strong transferability across different LLM backbones.

[Opinion dynamics under electoral shocks in competitive campaigns](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04829)

- MDVM-ES: introduces a computational framework based on the Voter model that integrates individual memory (persistence) and abrupt electoral shocks (external perturbation) to model opinion dynamics in competitive campaigns.
- The model simulates how voter inertia, determined by memory length m, competes with the intensity $p_s$ and duration $\Delta t$ of the shock to influence transient and stationary electoral outcomes.
- Results show that memory enhances system resilience against shocks, while strong, timely shocks can abruptly realign collective preferences, leading to phase-like regions of stability or realignment in the parameter space.

[Safe Urban Traffic Control via Uncertainty-Aware Conformal Prediction and World-Model Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04821)

- STREAM-RL: introduces a unified framework for safe urban traffic control, integrating PU-GAT+ (uncertainty-aware forecasting), CRFN-BY (dependence-robust anomaly detection), and LyCon-WRL+ (certified safe RL).
- The framework propagates calibrated uncertainty from forecasting through anomaly detection to safe policy learning, providing end-to-end theoretical guarantees for coverage, False Discovery Rate (FDR) control, and Lyapunov stability.
- STREAM-RL achieves high coverage efficiency (91.4%), controls FDR at 4.1% under verified dependence, and significantly improves the safety rate (95.2%) compared to standard PPO (69%).

---

[Properties of the core and other solution concepts of Bel coalitional games in the ex-ante scenario](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04817)

- Bel Coalitional Games (BCG): studies the properties of the core and other solution concepts in coalitional games that incorporate uncertainty using belief functions and Choquet integrals, focusing on the ex-ante scenario where contracts are evaluated before uncertainty resolution.
- The research investigates the geometrical structure of the ex-ante core, finding it is an affine space when agents share a common prior probability distribution.
- The paper defines ex-ante versions of the prenucleolus, kernel, and bargaining set, demonstrating that the classical inclusion relations among these solution concepts hold in this uncertain environment.

---

[Agentic Al in Healthcare & Medicine: A Seven-Dimensional Taxonomy for Empirical Evaluation of LLM-based Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04813)

- Seven-Dimensional Taxonomy (SDT): introduces an integrated taxonomy for the empirical evaluation of 49 LLM-based agents in healthcare and medicine, covering Cognitive Capabilities, Knowledge Management, Interaction Patterns, Adaptation & Learning, Safety & Ethics, Framework Typology, and Core Tasks & Subtasks.
- The taxonomy uses 7 core dimensions and 29 operational sub-dimensions to characterize agent maturity across implementation levels (Fully Implemented, Partially Implemented, Not Implemented).
- Empirical analysis reveals high maturity in retrieval-grounded advising (External Knowledge Integration, Medical Question Answering) but significant gaps in Adaptation & Learning and robust Safety & Ethics mechanisms.

---

[SE-BENCH: Benchmarking Self-Evolution with Knowledge Internalization](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04811)

- SE-BENCH (Benchmarking Self-Evolution with Knowledge Internalization): introduces a diagnostic environment that uses a Knowledge Obfuscation Mechanism to create a novel library (ZWC) for testing LLM agents' ability to internalize new knowledge, isolated from prior knowledge and reasoning complexity.
- The benchmark construction pipeline involves Obfuscation of NumPy functions, Generation of single- and multi-function coding tasks, and strict Consensus Filtering using multiple LLMs (Qwen3-coder, GPT-OSS, Gemini 2.5-PRO).
- Experiments reveal the Open-Book Paradox, where documentation inhibits retention, and the RL Gap, showing standard RL fails to internalize new knowledge due to PPO clipping and negative gradients, favoring Closed-SFT.

---

[Beyond Rewards in Reinforcement Learning for Cyber Defence](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04809)

- Ground Truth Evaluation Framework for ACD Reward Functions (GTEF-ACD-RF): introduces a novel ground truth scoring mechanism to evaluate Autonomous Cyber Defence (ACD) agents trained with various sparse and dense reward functions in cyber gym environments (YT, CAGE 2).
- The evaluation uses the $Score_{GT}$ metric, which captures the maximum number of compromised nodes during an intra-step, enabling accurate, risk-aware comparison independent of the training reward structure.
- The research demonstrates that agents trained with sparse reward functions, particularly Sparse Positive-Negative (SPN), achieve superior performance, higher reliability, and lower worst-case risks compared to conventional dense rewards.

---

[SQP-Based Cable-Tension Allocation for Multi-Drone Load Transport](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04801)

- SQP-Based Tension Allocation: introduces a real-time optimization layer that improves a hierarchical load-position-attitude controller by incorporating a Sequential Quadratic Programming (SQP) algorithm.
- The SQP formulation minimizes squared cable tensions and includes a cable-alignment penalty to ensure balanced energy distribution and prevent tether convergence, thereby enhancing safety.
- Integrated into a four-layer MAATS controller, the SQP allocator achieves centimeter-level trajectory tracking accuracy and maintains safe inter-cable angles in real-time simulations.

---

[LALM-as-a-Judge: Benchmarking Large Audio-Language Models for Safety Evaluation in Multi-Turn Spoken Dialogues](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04796)

- LALM-as-a-Judge (Large Audio-Language Models as Safety Judges): introduces the first controlled benchmark and systematic study of LALMs as safety judges for multi-turn spoken dialogues, utilizing a Controlled Unsafe Dialogue Generation pipeline, various LALM Judges (Qwen2-Audio, Audio Flamingo 3, MERLION), a LLaMA Judge, multiple Input Modalities, Transcription Sources, and Prompting Strategies to produce a Safety Score Output.
- The approach generates 24,000 synthetic unsafe dialogues by replacing a single turn in safe dialogues using GPT-4o for text revision and TTS for audio synthesis, enabling fine-grained attribution of safety judgments across eight harmful categories and five severity grades.
- The benchmark evaluates judges based on Sensitivity (detecting unsafe content), Specificity (ordering severity levels), and Position Bias (stability across dialogue turns) to characterize architecture- and modality-dependent trade-offs.

---

[Active Asymmetric Multi-Agent Multimodal Learning under Uncertainty](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04763)

- A2MAML: introduces a principled three-stage approach for uncertainty-aware, modality-level collaboration, including stochastic local encoding, uncertainty-guided active selection, and asymmetric Bayesian aggregation.
- The framework models each modality-specific feature as a stochastic estimate with uncertainty prediction, actively selects reliable agent-modality pairs using a lightweight MLP selection policy, and aggregates information via Bayesian inverse-variance weighting.
- A2MAML is validated on connected autonomous driving scenarios for collaborative accident detection, achieving up to 18.7% higher detection rates compared to baselines under sensor corruption.

---

[Rationality Measurement and Theory for Reinforcement Learning Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04737)

- RMF: introduces a suite of rationality measures and associated theory for reinforcement learning agents, decomposing the Rational Risk Gap into extrinsic and intrinsic components.
- The extrinsic rational gap is upper bounded by the 1-Wasserstein distance between transition kernels and initial state distributions, quantifying environment shifts between training and deployment.
- The intrinsic rational gap is upper bounded by the empirical Rademacher complexity of the value function class, reflecting the algorithm's generalisability in a dynamic environment.

[SUPPORTING SOFTWARE ENGINEERING TASKS WITH AGENTIC AI: DEMONSTRATION ON DOCUMENT RETRIEVAL AND TEST SCENARIO GENERATION](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04726)

- Agentic AI Solutions for SE Tasks (TSG and DPR): introduces two LLM-based agentic AI architectures—one for automatic test scenario generation (TSG) using a star topology of specialized agents, and one for document processing and retrieval (DPR) using a delegator agent managing specialized worker agents.
- The TSG solution employs six agents, including a Retriever Agent, a Test Scenario Writer Agent, and a Fact Checker Agent, which utilizes a feedback loop to mitigate LLM hallucination by verifying output against the Functional Specification Document (FSD).
- The DPR solution provides a common interface (App) for four use cases (Search, Q&A, Trace, Reading), where an LLM-driven Delegator Agent routes user requests to the appropriate specialized LLM-based worker agent, all sharing a Qdrant document database.

[AGILE: Hand-Object Interaction Reconstruction from Video via Agentic Generation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04672)

- AGILE: introduces a robust framework that shifts the paradigm from reconstruction to agentic generation for hand-object interaction (HOI) learning, utilizing a VLM agent for supervision, multi-view synthesis, 3D lifting, mesh refinement, and contact-aware optimization.
- The approach eliminates the dependency on brittle Structure-from-Motion (SfM) initialization by employing a robust anchor-and-track strategy, initializing object pose at a single interaction onset frame (IOF) using a foundation model.
- AGILE generates simulation-ready assets with watertight geometry and high-fidelity textures by integrating semantic, geometric, and interaction stability constraints to enforce physical plausibility during tracking.

---

[Towards Structured, State-Aware, and Execution-Grounded Reasoning for Software Engineering Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04640)

- Structured, State-Aware, and Execution-Grounded SE Agent: introduces a paradigm shift for Software Engineering (SE) agents, moving from reactive behavior to structured reasoning by incorporating explicit state management, execution feedback integration, and tool use.
- The architecture utilizes an LLM Agent that reads and updates a structured State component, which persistently stores hypotheses, invariants, and dependencies, enabling coherent long-horizon reasoning.
- This approach aims to overcome limitations of reactive agents, such as inconsistent reasoning and forgotten assumptions, by treating reasoning as the evolution of an internal state rather than repeated reconstruction from prompt history.

[Relational Scene Graphs for Object Grounding of Natural Language Commands](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04635)

- Relational Scene Graph Grounding Pipeline: introduces an LLM-based pipeline that leverages 3D Scene Graphs (3DSGs) enhanced with explicit spatial edges (closed- or open-vocabulary) to ground natural language commands to target objects in robotic environments.
- The approach uses a VLM-Based Edge Generation Pipeline to infer open-vocabulary spatial relations between objects from robot-captured images, which are then added as edges to the 3DSG structure.
- Experiments using GPT-4o and GPT-5 demonstrate that incorporating explicit spatial edges significantly improves LLM performance in target object grounding, with GPT-5 achieving up to 99.5% accuracy on the VLA-3D dataset.

[WIDESEEK-R1: Exploring Width Scaling for Broad Information Seeking via Multi-Agent Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04634)

- WIDESEEK-R1: introduces a hierarchical lead-agent-subagent system trained via MARL to synergize scalable orchestration and parallel execution for broad information seeking.
- The system utilizes a shared LLM where the Lead Agent decomposes tasks using the call_subagent tool, and parallel Subagents execute subtasks using search and access tools within isolated contexts.
- The training employs a MARL objective based on GRPO, incorporating dual-level advantage reweighting and group-normalized advantage assignment to enable effective width scaling.

[VILLAIN at AVerImaTeC: Verifying Image–Text Claims via Multi-Agent Collaboration](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04587)

- VILLAIN (Verifying Image-text claims via MuLti-Agent collabo-ratIoN): introduces a multimodal fact-checking system that verifies image-text claims through prompt-based multi-agent collaboration, including Evidence Retrieval (retrieving evidence from knowledge stores), Evidence Analysis (distilling evidence via VLM agents), Question-Answer Generation (synthesizing analysis into QA pairs), and Verdict Prediction (producing the final verification outcome).- The system employs five VLM agents (Text-Text $A_{TT}$, Image-Text $A_{IT}$, Cross-Modal $A_{CM}$, QA Generation $A_{QA}$, Verdict Prediction $A_{V}$) based on Gemini-2.5-Pro to handle modality-specific analysis, iterative QA generation, and final verdict prediction.
- Evidence retrieval is enhanced by reranking and a URL Content Extraction Pipeline that uses browser automation (Playwright/Chromium) to fill missing textual content in the knowledge stores ($K^{txt}, K^{img}$).

[Reinforcement Learning-based Home Energy Management with Heterogeneous Batteries and Stochastic EV Behaviour](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04578)

- DRL-HEMS Framework: introduces a novel home energy management system based on deep reinforcement learning formulated as a constrained Markov decision process (CMDP) and solved via a Lagrangian soft actor-critic (SAC) algorithm.
- The framework jointly minimizes net grid electricity and battery degradation costs while strictly satisfying occupant thermal comfort and EV charging requirements under stochastic uncertainties.
- The approach explicitly incorporates heterogeneous degradation models for stationary (LFP) and EV (NMC) batteries alongside realistic stochastic modeling of EV user behavior derived from travel survey data.

[Vibe AIGC: A New Paradigm for Content Generation via Agentic Orchestration](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04575)

- Vibe AIGC: introduces a new paradigm for content generation via agentic orchestration, transforming high-level human intent (Vibe) into executable, verifiable multi-agent pipelines using a Meta Planner, supported by a Domain-Specific Expert Knowledge Base and Human-in-the-Loop mechanisms.
- The architecture adopts a hierarchical orchestration strategy, where the Meta Planner acts as a System Architect, generating a macro-level SOP blueprint (Creative Layer) and configuring the detailed workflow graph (Algorithmic Layer) for execution by specialized AI Agents and Foundation Models.
- This system aims to bridge the Intent-Execution Gap by shifting the user's role from "Prompt Engineer" to "Commander," delegating low-level technical implementation to autonomous, recursive multi-agent workflows.

[Control protocols for harmonically confined run-and-tumble particles](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04560)

- RTP-CPO: introduces a systematic theory for optimal control protocols in active matter systems by reformulating the Run-and-Tumble Particle (RTP) dynamics as an infinite hierarchy of ordinary differential equations, enabling the analytical determination of control parameters (tumbling rate and stiffness) for finite-time transformations.
- The approach is used to find "shortcuts" between prescribed nonequilibrium steady states, focusing on the long protocol duration limit where analytical solutions for optimal protocols minimizing mechanical work are derived using Euler-Lagrange equations.
- Analysis of optimal protocols reveals that efficient compression or expansion relies on abrupt changes in the confinement strength and strategic modulation of particle activity (tumbling rate) to exploit persistent outward motion.

[PERSOPILOT: AN ADAPTIVE AI-COPILOT FOR TRANSPARENT CONTEXTUALIZED PERSONA CLASSIFICATION AND PERSONALIZED RESPONSE GENERATION](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04540)

- PersoPilot: introduces an adaptive AI-Copilot framework that integrates persona understanding with contextual analysis to support both end users and analysts through a dynamic feedback loop.
- The framework consists of two primary modules, PersoAgent for real-time user interaction and personalized recommendation, and Analytic Tools for analyst-driven labeling and model refinement.
- PersoPilot utilizes a BERT-based Persona Extractor and an OpenAI LLM within PersoAgent, alongside a Phi-4 mini-instruct LLM and a TF-IDF classifier within Analytic Tools, to enable transparent, reasoning-augmented personalization and continuous active learning.

[Choice via AI](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04526)

- AIC (AI Agent's Choice): introduces a choice theoretic model where an AI Agent makes recommendations by maximizing a Strict Preference Relation over an interpreted choice menu defined by an Interpretation Operator.
- The model addresses whether AI recommendations are rational and aligned with the Decision Maker's preferences, considering potential misinterpretations of the choice menu, often based on LLMs.
- Key extensions include RAIC (Rational AIC) requiring Double Monotonicity for full identifiability, and GRAIC (Grounded and Rational AIC) requiring Idempotence and satisfying the Weak Axiom of Revealed Preference (WARP).

---

[Learning the Value Systems of Agents with Preference-based and Inverse Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04518)

- VSLF: introduces a novel method to automatically learn agent value systems from observations and human demonstrations, formalizing the problem using Multi-Objective Markov Decision Processes (MOMDPs).
- The framework splits the learning process into Value Grounding Learning (VGL) to infer value alignment functions and Value System Identification (VSI) to infer agent-specific linear aggregation functions.
- VGL uses Preference-based Inverse Reinforcement Learning (PbIRL) with quantitative trajectory comparisons, while VSI uses Deep Maximum Entropy IRL based on observed optimal trajectories.

[OSCAgent: Accelerating the Discovery of Organic Solar Cells with LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04510)

- OSCAgent: introduces a multi-agent framework for Organic Solar Cell (OSC) acceptor discovery that unifies retrieval-augmented design, molecular generation, and systematic evaluation into a continuously improving pipeline.
- The framework utilizes three collaborative LLM agents—Planner, Generator, and Experimenter—to guide exploration, propose novel molecules, and assess candidates based on predicted Power Conversion Efficiency (PCE), synthetic accessibility, and electronic properties.
- Candidate evaluation is enhanced by a multimodal PCE predictor incorporating uncertainty quantification and auxiliary HOMO/LUMO prediction tasks, ensuring chemically valid and high-performing molecular designs.

[ReThinker: Scientific Reasoning by Rethinking with Guided Reflection and Confidence Control](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04496)

- ReThinker: introduces an uncertainty-gated agentic framework that orchestrates retrieval, tool use, and multi-agent reasoning through a stage-wise Solver (Iterative reasoning synthesis)-Critic (Guided reflection, refinement)-Selector (Uncertainty aggregation, selection) architecture.
- The framework dynamically allocates computation based on model confidence, enabling adaptive tool invocation, guided multi-dimensional reflection, and robust confidence-weighted selection for expert-level scientific reasoning.
- ReThinker utilizes a reverse data synthesis pipeline and adaptive trajectory recycling strategy to transform successful reasoning traces into high-quality supervision for scalable training without human annotation.

[ProAgentBench: Evaluating LLM Agents for Proactive Assistance with Real-World Data](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04482)

- ProAgentBench: introduces a rigorous benchmark for proactive agents, utilizing a Hierarchical Pipeline (Two-stage evaluation) that decomposes assistance into timing prediction and content generation, evaluated using real-world data collected via LifeTrace (Data collection tool).
- The benchmark addresses deficiencies in existing datasets by providing 28,000+ events from 500+ hours of continuous real user sessions, capturing authentic bursty interaction patterns and pre-assistance behavioral context.
- Experiments reveal that incorporating long-term user context via memory-based methods like RAG, Knowledge Graph, and Cluster-Based Persona Memory significantly enhances LLM prediction accuracy for proactive assistance tasks.

[What's in a Benchmark? The Case of SWE-Bench in Automated Program Repair](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04449)

- SWE-Bench Ecosystem Analysis: introduces a comprehensive study of 212 submissions to the SWE-Bench Lite and Verified leaderboards, examining submitter origins, product characteristics, and LLM usage in Automated Program Repair (APR).
- The analysis reveals that submissions achieving the highest precision (up to 76.8% Resolved) predominantly rely on proprietary LLMs, particularly the Claude 4 family.
- The study highlights the dominance of industry submissions, the competitive performance of emerging open-source tools, and critical issues regarding transparency and patch overfitting in the benchmark ecosystem.

[AgenticAKM : Enroute to Agentic Architecture Knowledge Management](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04445)

- AgenticAKM: introduces an agentic approach for Architecture Knowledge Management (AKM) that decomposes architecture recovery and documentation into manageable sub-tasks handled by specialized agents.
- The system employs four distinct types of specialized agents—Extractor, Retriever, Generator, and Validator—coordinated by a central Orchestrator to ensure iterative refinement and high-quality output.
- Validation through a user study comparing AgenticAKM against a baseline single LLM call demonstrates that the agentic approach produces significantly better Architecture Decision Records (ADRs).

[MaMa: A Game-Theoretic Approach for Designing Safe Agentic Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04431)

- MaMa: introduces a novel algorithm for designing safe agentic systems by formalizing the problem as a Stackelberg security game between a Meta-Agent (system designer) and a Meta-Adversary (worst-case attacker), utilizing LLM-based adversarial search.
- The Meta-Agent iteratively proposes system designs, incorporating defenses based on feedback from the Meta-Adversary, which searches for and evaluates the strongest attacks by compromising a subset of agents.
- Systems designed using MaMa demonstrate significantly improved safety against worst-case adversarial attacks while maintaining high task performance compared to systems optimized solely for quality.

[SPEAR: An Engineering Case Study of Multi-Agent Coordination for Smart Contract Auditing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04418)

- SPEAR (Strategic Planning, Execution, and Automated Repair): introduces a multi-agent coordination framework for autonomous smart contract auditing, utilizing specialized agents for planning, execution, repair, command execution, and coordination.
- The framework employs established Multi-Agent System (MAS) patterns, including Contract Net, Plan Negotiation, and Resource Auction protocols, to enable distributed decision-making, self-healing, and resource arbitration under partial observability.
- SPEAR's Repair Agent implements a programmatic-first repair (PFIR) policy, prioritizing deterministic fixes over costly generative LLM invocations to recover from brittle generated artifacts.

---

[EMA Policy Gradient: Taming Reinforcement Learning for LLMs with EMA Anchor and Top-k KL](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04417)

- EMA Policy Gradient (EMA-PG): introduces two techniques—an EMA anchor and a Top-k KL estimator—to stabilize and improve policy gradient algorithms for LLMs.
- The EMA anchor replaces the fixed anchor policy ($\pi_{ref}$) with an Exponential Moving Average ($\pi_{\theta_{ema}}$) of the policy weights, similar to a target network in deep Q-learning, to provide stable supervision targets.
- The Top-k KL estimator combines exact KL computed on the top-k logit indices with a masked sampled KL correction for the tail distribution, yielding unbiased KL values and gradients with low memory footprint.

[Self-evolving Embodied AI](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04411)

- Self-evolving Embodied AI: introduces a new paradigm where agents operate based on their changing state and dynamic environment, utilizing memory self-updating, task self-switching, environment self-prediction, embodiment self-adaptation, and model self-evolution to achieve continually adaptive intelligence.
- This framework enables embodied AI to transition from human-crafted settings to in-the-wild settings characterized by variable embodiments and dynamic open environments.
- The system operates through a unified evolutionary loop driven by the agent's self-state transitions and action-feedback interactions, coordinating the co-evolution of all five core components across multiple time scales.

---

[Optimal Rates for Feasible Payoff Set Estimation in Games](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04397)

- FPS Estimation Framework: introduces a learning framework to estimate the entire feasible payoff set (FPS) of matrices consistent with observed equilibrium behavior in bimatrix games, using the Learner, Two Players, Bimatrix Game, Strategy Profiles, Action Samples, Empirical Strategy Profiles, Feasible Payoff Set, Hausdorff Distance, Precision Level, Risk Parameter, and Approximation Parameter components.
- The research provides the first minimax-optimal sample complexity rates for estimating the FPS up to Hausdorff error $\epsilon$, covering both exact ($\alpha=0$) and approximate ($\alpha>0$) Nash equilibria in general-sum and zero-sum games.
- The analysis shows that the problem is ill-posed for exact equilibria unless strategies have minimum probability ($\pi_{\min}>0$), and small approximation values $\alpha$ substantially degrade the optimal rates due to unavoidable dependence on $\alpha^{-1}$.

[Safe and Stylized Trajectory Planning for Autonomous Driving via Diffusion Model](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04329)

- SDD Planner (Stylish Diffusion Drive Planner): introduces a diffusion-based framework for safe and stylized trajectory planning, integrating a Multi-Source Style-Aware Encoder and a Style-Guided Dynamic Trajectory Generator.
- The Multi-Source Style-Aware Encoder uses distance-sensitive attention to fuse heterogeneous inputs into stylized features ($Z_{style}$) for heterogeneous safety-style perception.
- The Style-Guided Dynamic Trajectory Generator employs a time-step adaptive classifier-guided diffusion mechanism to dynamically reconcile safety constraints and user-preferred driving styles.

[FROM ASSUMPTIONS TO ACTIONS: TURNING LLM REASONING INTO UNCERTAINTY-AWARE PLANNING FOR EMBODIED AGENTS](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04326)

- PCE (Planner-Composer-Evaluator): introduces a modular framework that converts fragmented assumptions latent in LLM reasoning traces into a structured decision tree for uncertainty-aware planning in embodied multi-agent systems.
- The framework utilizes a Planner (LLM component) to generate reasoning traces, a Composer (LLM component) to structure assumptions into a decision tree, and an Evaluator (LLM component) to score scenarios based on likelihood, gain, and cost.
- PCE consistently outperforms communication-centric baselines by explicitly treating environmental assumptions as first-class decision variables, enabling rational action selection with minimal communication overhead.
