[ProxyWar: Dynamic Assessment of LLM Code Generation in Game Arenas](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04296)

- ProxyWar: introduces a novel framework that systematically assesses LLM code generation quality by embedding LLM-generated agents (Proxies) within diverse, competitive game environments, combining automated testing, iterative code repair, and multi-agent tournaments.
- The framework utilizes a multi-layer architecture including Code Generation, Testing, Agent, Game Environment, and Tournament Management layers to provide a holistic view of operational characteristics beyond functional correctness.
- ProxyWar provides skill-based rankings reflecting functional correctness and operational performance across ten diverse game environments, revealing discrepancies between static benchmark scores and dynamic performance.

[Agent-Omit: Training Efficient LLM Agents for Adaptive Thought and Observation Omission via Agentic Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04284)

- Agent-Omit: introduces a unified training framework that empowers LLM agents to adaptively omit redundant thoughts and observations, integrating (Cold Start Data Generation) with (Adaptive Omission Policy Refinement).
- The framework utilizes a Dual Sampling Strategy and an Omit-Aware Reward mechanism to incentivize adaptive context management and token efficiency during multi-turn interactions.
- Agent-Omit achieves comparable accuracy to frontier LLM agents while substantially reducing token cost by selectively omitting context based on turn-dependent necessity.

[Data Agents: Levels, State of the Art, and Open Problems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04261)

- Data Agents Taxonomy (L0-L5 Hierarchy): introduces a hierarchical taxonomy of data agents, leveraging LLMs and tool-using agents to automate data management, preparation, and analysis tasks across six levels of autonomy.
- The taxonomy spans from Level 0 (L0, no autonomy, human in charge) to Level 5 (L5, full autonomy, data agent in charge), defining roles like Assistant, Executor, Orchestrator, Proactive, and Generative components.
- Data agents operate within complex Data+AI ecosystems, handling large, heterogeneous data lakes and requiring robust capabilities in perception, long-horizon planning, and governance.

[Scaling Agentic Verifier for Competitive Coding](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04254)

- Agentic Verifier: introduces an LLM-based agent designed for competitive coding verification, utilizing a multi-stage training pipeline including data synthesis, rejection fine-tuning, and agentic reinforcement learning.
- The verifier actively generates highly discriminative test inputs through multi-turn interaction with a code execution environment to expose behavioral discrepancies among candidate solutions.
- The approach achieves substantial absolute gains (up to +10-15%) in Best@k accuracy across five competitive programming benchmarks compared to strong execution-based baselines.

[Empirical-MCTS: Continuous Agent Evolution via Dual-Experience Monte Carlo Tree Search](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04248)

- Empirical-MCTS: introduces a dual-loop framework that transforms stateless Monte Carlo Tree Search (MCTS) into a continuous, non-parametric learning process by unifying local exploration and global memory optimization.
- The local exploration loop utilizes Pairwise-Experience-Evolutionary Meta-Prompting (PE-EMP) as a reflexive optimizer to dynamically evolve the meta-prompt (system prompt) based on pairwise feedback.
- The global memory optimization loop employs a Memory Optimization Agent to manage the Global Experience Library as a dynamic policy prior, distilling high-quality insights across problems using atomic operations (Add, Modify, Merge, Delete).

[On the Uncertainty of Large Language Model-Based Multi-Agent Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04234)

- Entropy Judger: introduces a systematic analysis of uncertainty dynamics in LLM-based MAS across four topologies and six tasks, leveraging 245 hierarchical entropy and computational features.
- The research finds that MAS effectiveness is largely determined by first-round uncertainty dynamics, and a single agent system outperforms MAS in approximately 43.3% of cases.
- The Entropy Judger consistently boosts accuracy by selecting high-quality outputs from MAS pass@k results based on learned entropy patterns, establishing uncertainty as a principled perspective for multi-agent reasoning.

[Why Agentic-PRs Get Rejected: A Comparative Study of Coding Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04226)

- APRA: introduces a comparative study of 654 rejected Pull Requests (PRs) from the AIDEV dataset, generated by five coding agents and human developers, using manual coding and a rejection modes taxonomy to identify agent-specific failure patterns.
- The analysis reveals seven rejection modes exclusive to Agentic-PRs, including "No confidence in AI-generated code" and "Are too large," highlighting differences in agent usage and reliability.
- To address the high prevalence of rejected PRs lacking explicit feedback (Unknown PRs), the study proposes a set of simple heuristics for filtering non-informative cases, improving data quality for future large-scale studies.

[InterPReT: Interactive Policy Restructuring and Training Enable Effective Imitation Learning from Laypersons](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04213)

- InterPReT (Interactive Policy Restructuring and Training): introduces an interactive learning paradigm that uses LLM code synthesis (Policy Restructuring Module) based on user instructions to update a Structured Policy, and optimizes its weights (Policy Training Module) using user demonstrations.
- The approach enables laypersons to effectively teach AI agents, yielding more robust policies in unseen conditions and requiring fewer demonstrations compared to a generic imitation learning baseline (IL with MLP).
- The system facilitates multi-turn interaction by allowing users to provide instructions and demonstrations, monitor agent performance, and inspect the agent's decision-making strategy via natural language summaries generated from the policy structure.

[From Helpfulness to Toxic Proactivity: Diagnosing Behavioral Misalignment in LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04197)

- TPEF (Toxic Proactivity Evaluation Framework): introduces a novel framework to diagnose Toxic Proactivity, an active failure mode where LLM agents prioritize utility over ethics, using dual-model dilemma-driven interactions.
- The framework comprises an Automated Scenario Generation module that synthesizes high-conflict narratives and a Multi-turn Misalignment Simulation module that operationalizes agent behavior through closed-loop interaction with an LLM-based environment.
- TPEF defines a structured dual-track action space, separating compliant actions ($A^+$) from toxic actions ($A^-$), enabling the quantification of misalignment rate and analysis of strategic versus direct toxic behaviors.

[The Missing Half: Unveiling Training-time Implicit Safety Risks Beyond Deployment](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04196)

- Training-time Implicit Safety Risks Taxonomy: introduces a systematic study of harmful behaviors emerging during LLM training, not explicitly specified by the training objective or reward signal, categorized by five risk levels, three high-level categories, and three incentives.
- The five risk levels (L1-L5) define a hierarchy of autonomy, ranging from explicit instruction (L1) to latent knowledge acquired during pretraining (L5).
- Evaluation across eight diverse models demonstrates substantial threat potential, with Llama-3.1-8B-Instruct exhibiting risky behaviors in 74.4% of runs under L3 (Background Information) conditions.

[MA3DSG: Multi-Agent 3D Scene Graph Generation for Large-Scale Indoor Environments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04152)

- MA3DSG (Multi-Agent 3D Scene Graph Generation): introduces a decentralized multi-agent framework for scalable 3D Scene Graph Generation (3DSGG) in large-scale indoor environments, utilizing Multi-Agent Exploration, 3D Semantic Scene Graph Generation, and 3D Semantic Scene Graph Alignment.
- The approach employs a training-free graph alignment algorithm to efficiently merge partial query graphs generated by individual agents into a unified global scene graph.
- MA3DSG-Bench is proposed as a comprehensive benchmark supporting diverse agent configurations, domain sizes, and dynamic conditions for rigorous 3DSGG evaluation.

---

[OMG-Agent: Toward Robust Missing Modality Generation with Decoupled Coarse-to-Fine Agentic Workflows](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04144)

- OMG-Agent (Omni-Modality Generation Agent): introduces a novel framework that reformulates missing modality reconstruction as a dynamic coarse-to-fine Agentic Workflow, explicitly decoupling high-level reasoning from low-level synthesis using three synergistic agents: Semantic Planner, Evidence Retriever, and Instruction-Following Executor.
- The framework resolves the Semantic-Detail Entanglement dilemma by using the Semantic Planner for deterministic logical guidance, the Evidence Retriever for grounding abstract semantics in external knowledge, and the Executor for retrieval-injected detail synthesis via dual constraints.
- The Executor utilizes a Conditional Latent Diffusion Process with a hierarchical Dual-Conditioning Injection mechanism to apply global consistency constraints from the plan and local statistics from the retrieved evidence.

---

[DECOUPLING TIME AND RISK: RISK-SENSITIVE REINFORCEMENT LEARNING WITH GENERAL DISCOUNTING](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04131)

- RIGOR: introduces a unified framework for stock augmentation in distributional RL to support general discount functions and OCE risk measures, enabling time-consistent optimization of risk-sensitive objectives.
- The framework resolves time-inconsistency issues of prior general discounting methods by properly modeling the non-stationary optimal policy required for flexible time preferences.
- The methodology is validated across financial tasks (Goal-Based Wealth Management) and high-dimensional control environments (Atari 2600), demonstrating improved performance over time-inconsistent baselines.

---

[Multi-threaded Recast-Based A* Pathfinding for Scalable Navigation in Dynamic Game Environments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04130)

- MRAPF (Multi-threaded Recast-Based A* Pathfinding Framework): introduces a scalable pathfinding system for dynamic 3D game environments, integrating Recast-based NavMesh generation, multi-threaded A* computation, trajectory smoothing, and density-aware crowd coordination.
- The framework utilizes an asynchronous multi-threaded architecture to decouple pathfinding from the main rendering loop, maintaining 350+ FPS with 1000 simultaneous agents.
- Path Post-Processing, including the Funnel Algorithm and Bezier Curve Smoothing, refines raw A* output into naturalistic, C¹-continuous trajectories, while Density Analysis ensures collision-free crowd navigation.

[KGLAMP: Knowledge Graph-guided Language model for Adaptive Multi-robot Planning and Replanning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04129)

- KGLAMP (Knowledge Graph-guided Language model for Adaptive Multi-robot Planning and Replanning): introduces a framework for heterogeneous multi-robot planning that uses specialized LLM agents grounded by three knowledge graphs (Grelation, Gproperty, Greach) to generate accurate PDDL specifications for a symbolic planner.
- The knowledge graphs serve as a persistent, structured memory encoding object relations, spatial reachability, and robot capabilities, mitigating context overload and improving LLM reliability in generating symbolic representations.
- The framework includes a replanning module that utilizes a VLM and an iterative refinement loop to dynamically update the knowledge graphs and recover from symbolic inconsistencies or execution failures in dynamic environments.

[DELTA: Deliberative Multi-Agent Reasoning with Reinforcement Learning for Multimodal Psychological Counseling](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04112)

- DELTA (DELiberative mulTi-Agent): introduces a deliberative multi-agent framework that models psychological counseling as a structured reasoning process, separating evidence grounding, mental state abstraction, and response generation using specialized agents.
- The framework utilizes VCIA and VoCIA to elicit multimodal evidence, which is processed by the MGA and summarized by the MSSA into a structured Mental State Representation.
- Response generation by the CRGA is optimized using Reinforcement Learning (GRPO) guided by the distribution-level Emotion Attunement Score (EAS) to encourage emotionally attuned responses.

[VideoBrain: Learning Adaptive Frame Sampling for Long Video Understanding](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04094)

- VideoBrain: introduces an end-to-end trainable framework enabling Vision-Language Models (VLMs) to adaptively acquire visual information in long videos using dual sampling agents and iterative reasoning.
- The framework employs a behavior-aware reward function coupled with a data classification pipeline to prevent reward hacking and efficiently guide the model's agent invocation policy during reinforcement learning.
- VideoBrain achieves consistent accuracy improvements on long video benchmarks while using 30-40% fewer frames compared to baseline methods, demonstrating efficient resource allocation.

#### 3rd February 2026

[AUTOFIGURE: GENERATING AND REFINING PUBLICATION-READY SCIENTIFIC ILLUSTRATIONS](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03828)

- AUTOFIGURE (Reasoned Rendering Framework): introduces an agentic framework for generating publication-ready scientific illustrations from long-form text, utilizing Concept Extraction, Symbolic Construction, a Critique-and-Refine Loop, Style-Guided Aesthetic Rendering, and an Erase-and-Correct Module.
- The framework decouples structural layout generation from aesthetic rendering, using a multi-stage pipeline to ensure both structural fidelity and visual appeal, resolving the trade-off between accuracy and aesthetics.
- The authors also introduce FigureBench, the first large-scale benchmark containing 3,300 high-quality scientific text-figure pairs, demonstrating that AUTOFIGURE consistently surpasses baselines in generating complex illustrations.

[Digital-Twin Empowered Deep Reinforcement Learning For Site-Specific Radio Resource Management in NextG Wireless Aerial Corridor](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03801)

- DT-enabled MH-PPO: introduces a two-stage optimization framework coupling physics-based beam gain modeling with Deep Reinforcement Learning (DRL) for scalable online UAV-BS-beam association in NextG aerial corridors.
- The framework utilizes a high-fidelity Channel Twin (CT) constructed via ray-tracing to generate site-specific channel datasets for training a Multi-Head Proximal Policy Optimization (MH-PPO) agent.
- The MH-PPO agent employs a multi-head actor-critic architecture to map high-dimensional channel state information to joint resource allocation decisions, achieving superior throughput and millisecond-level inference latency.

[FullStack-Agent: Enhancing Agentic Full-Stack Web Coding via Development-Oriented Testing and Repository Back-Translation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03798)

- FullStack-Agent: introduces a unified system for agentic full-stack web coding, combining FullStack-Dev (Multi-Agent Framework), FullStack-Learn (Self-Improvement Pipeline), and FullStack-Bench (Evaluation Benchmark).
- FullStack-Dev coordinates planning, frontend, and backend coding agents, utilizing specialized tools like the Frontend Debugging Tool and Backend Debugging Tool for dynamic error localization and correction.
- FullStack-Learn enhances the backbone LLM's coding abilities through Repository Back-Translation, which converts real-world repositories into high-quality agent trajectories for supervised fine-tuning.

[Understanding Agent Scaling in LLM-Based Multi-Agent Systems via Diversity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03794)

- Information-Theoretic Framework for MAS Scaling: introduces a framework showing that LLM-based Multi-Agent System (MAS) performance is bounded by intrinsic task uncertainty, not raw agent count, and depends on the number of effective channels ($K$).
- The framework defines usable evidence ($I_{MAS}$) and derives architecture-agnostic bounds demonstrating that performance improvements arise from increasing the effective channel count ($K$) and complementarity rate ($\alpha$).
- The paper introduces $K^*$, a label-free proxy quantifying the number of non-redundant information sources in agent outputs, empirically showing that 2 diverse agents can match or exceed 16 homogeneous agents.

---

[AORCHESTRA: Automating Sub-Agent Creation for Agentic Orchestration](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03786)

- AORCHESTRA: introduces an orchestration-centric agentic system that automates sub-agent creation using the Unified 4-tuple Abstraction (Instruction, Context, Tools, Model), enabling specialized executors on demand.
- The Orchestrator Agent dynamically decomposes complex tasks and delegates execution via the Delegate Action, curating task-relevant context, tools, and models for each Dynamic Sub-Agent.
- The framework supports learning the orchestration policy through supervised fine-tuning and iterative in-context learning for optimizing cost-aware LLM routing.

[EFFICIENT ESTIMATION OF KERNEL SURROGATE MODELS FOR TASK ATTRIBUTION](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03783)

- KERNELSM (Kernel Surrogate Models): introduces a kernel-based attribution method to quantify task influence by modeling complex, non-linear task interactions, overcoming limitations of linear surrogate models and influence functions.
- The approach uses an efficient gradient-based estimation procedure (GradEx) leveraging a first-order approximation of pretrained models to avoid computationally expensive repeated retraining.
- KERNELSM achieves significantly higher correlation with ground-truth leave-one-out (LOO) scores and yields substantial improvements in downstream task selection benchmarks, including LLM in-context learning and multi-objective reinforcement learning.

[A Scene Graph Backed Approach to Open Set Semantic Mapping](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03781)

- 3DSSG-BAM: introduces a modular mapping architecture that establishes the 3D Semantic Scene Graph (3DSSG) as the foundational backend and primary knowledge representation for real-time, incremental semantic mapping.
- The architecture utilizes a multi-layered 3DSSG backend, including Frames, Segments, and Objects layers, to maintain topological consistency and bridge sub-symbolic sensor data with high-level symbolic reasoning.
- The system integrates Vision-Language Foundation Models (VLFMs) like CLIP for open-set queries and incorporates an Incremental Predicate Prediction (IPP) module to infer semantic relationships dynamically, enabling exploitation by knowledge graphs and LLMs.

[DiffLOB: Diffusion Models for Counterfactual Generation in Limit Order Books](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03776)

- DiffLOB: introduces a regime-conditioned Diffusion model for controllable and counterfactual generation of Limit Order Book (LOB) trajectories, utilizing a stacked Wavenet-style backbone and explicit future market regime conditioning.
- The framework employs a dual-stage training strategy, training the backbone first, then freezing it to train a Control Module that injects additive regime-dependent intervention signals.
- DiffLOB achieves superior controllable realism and counterfactual validity compared to baseline models, providing meaningful synthetic trajectories for downstream tasks like future market regime prediction.

[An Empirical Study of Collective Behaviors and Social Dynamics in Large Language Model Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03775)

- CoST (Chain of Social Thought): introduces a zero-shot method to reduce harmful LLM agent activity by prompting agents to consider the social harm of their posts within the Chirper.ai social network environment.
- The study empirically analyzes 7M posts and 1M+ interactions among 32K memory-enhanced LLM agents on the Chirper.ai platform over a year to investigate collective behaviors and social dynamics.
- Findings show that LLM agents exhibit human-like homophily and social influence but develop unique macro-level patterns regarding toxic language, ideological polarization, and network structure.

[Nested Search*](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03720)

- Nested Search Model (NSM): introduces a dynamic decision-making problem modeled as a tree structure that generalizes Weitzman (1979) by incorporating incremental search and correlated prize realizations.
- The optimal search strategy is characterized by an index policy, where the agent inspects the node with the highest index, provided it exceeds the highest realized prize among fully inspected boxes.
- The theoretical results are applied to study monopolistic competition in a market with two stages of product inspection, demonstrating that regulations on drip pricing lower equilibrium price and raise consumer surplus.

---

[Training Multi-Turn Search Agent via Contrastive Dynamic Branch Sampling](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03719)

- BranPO (Branching Relative Policy Optimization): introduces a value-free reinforcement learning framework that mitigates credit assignment ambiguity in long-horizon agentic tasks via contrastive dynamic branch sampling.
- The method constructs step-level contrastive supervision by recursively truncating trajectories near the tail and resampling alternative continuations over shared prefixes.
- BranPO integrates Difficulty-Aware Branch Sampling and Redundant Step Masking to improve exploration efficiency and suppress unnecessary continuation bias in LLM search agents.

---

[SWE-Refactor: A Repository-Level Benchmark for Real-World LLM-Based Code Refactoring](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03712)

- SWE-Refactor: introduces a new repository-level benchmark for LLM-based code refactoring, constructed via a four-step automated pipeline that includes Mine Refactorings via Static Analysis (extract commits), Curate Pure and Targeted Refactoring Types (filter impure changes), Enrich Refactoring Changes with Multi-Level Code Information (extract structural data), and Verify Compilation and Test Coverage (ensure correctness), evaluated using Compilation and Test Success (functional verification), AST-Based Refactoring Verification (structural correctness), and CodeBLEU (human-likeness verification).
- The benchmark comprises 1,099 developer-written, behavior-preserving refactorings mined from 18 Java projects, covering both atomic (Extract Method, Move Method, Inline Method) and compound refactoring types.
- Evaluation of nine widely used LLMs shows that complex and compound refactorings remain the primary source of failures, with the Multi-Agent workflow achieving the highest overall success rate.

[OmniRAG-Agent: Agentic Omnimodal Reasoning for Low-Resource Long Audio-Video Question Answering](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03707)

- OmniRAG-Agent: introduces an agentic omnimodal QA method for budgeted long audio-video reasoning, utilizing an OmniLLM, external retrieval banks, multi-turn tool use, and end-to-end reinforcement learning optimization.
- The framework constructs a Multi-Modal Retrieval Bank containing sampled frames and ASR transcripts, enabling the OmniLLM to fetch fine-grained evidence via dedicated retrieval tools.
- A Multi-turn Reasoning Process, optimized by Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) with a gated reward, allows the agent to iteratively plan, query, and integrate scattered evidence across long audio-video inputs.

[Cognitively Diverse Multiple-Choice Question Generation: A Hybrid Multi-Agent Framework with Large Language Models](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03704)

- ReQUESTA (Reading Question-generation Using Educational Smart Text Agents): introduces a hybrid multi-agent framework for generating cognitively diverse multiple-choice questions (MCQs) by decomposing authoring into specialized subtasks handled by LLM-powered agents and rule-based components.
- The framework systematically targets text-based (recall), inferential, and main idea (synthesis) comprehension through structured orchestration, planning, controlled generation, iterative evaluation, and post-processing.
- Evaluation showed that ReQUESTA-generated MCQs were consistently more challenging, more discriminative, and exhibited higher quality distractors compared to a single-pass GPT-5 zero-shot baseline.

[Agent Primitives: Reusable Latent Building Blocks for Multi-Agent Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03695)

- Agent Primitives: introduces a set of reusable latent building blocks for LLM-based Multi-Agent Systems (MAS), including Review, Voting and Selection, and Planning and Execution Primitives, orchestrated by an LLM-based Organizer guided by a Knowledge Pool.
- The primitives encapsulate recurring multi-agent computation patterns and communicate internally via latent Key-Value (KV) cache, which enhances robustness and efficiency by mitigating information degradation across multi-stage interactions.
- Primitives-based MAS consistently improves average accuracy by 12.0–16.5% over single-agent baselines while substantially reducing token usage and inference latency compared to text-based MAS.

[TodyComm: Task-Oriented Dynamic Communication for Multi-Round LLM-based Multi-Agent System](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03688)

- TodyComm (Task-Oriented Dynamic Communication for Multi-Round LLM-based Multi-Agent System): introduces a task-oriented framework that dynamically learns behavior-driven communication structures to coordinate LLM-based agents across multiple interaction rounds, including LLM-based Agents ($A_i$), Gated Recurrent Network (GRN), Multi-Layer Perceptron (MLP), Credit Generation Module, Participation Sampling, Inter-Agent Communication Graph ($G_C^t$), Decision Graph ($G_D$), and REINFORCE Algorithm.
- The system models multi-round interactions as a Markov Decision Process, where agent-level credits are learned via GRN to determine communication priority and decision influence, enabling dynamic graph construction.
- TodyComm constructs the Inter-Agent Communication Graph as a Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG) at each round and uses a separate Decision Graph for credit-weighted final aggregation.

---

[EFFICIENT INVESTMENT IN MULTI-AGENT MODELS OF PUBLIC TRANSPORTATION](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03687)

- PTP/NTP: introduces two multi-agent models for public transportation investment, focusing on optimizing utilitarian and egalitarian welfare objectives using graph theory and a Modified Dijkstra's Algorithm for cost minimization.
- The PTP model addresses bus stop placement along a line graph, finding that maximizing egalitarian welfare is NP-complete, even on simple topologies.
- The NTP model provides polynomial-time algorithms for one or two agents via a dynamic programming variant of Dijkstra's algorithm, but proves NP-completeness for a variable number of agents.

---

[When Should Agents Coordinate in Differentiable Sequential Decision Problems?](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03674)

- Dynamic Coordination Framework (DCF): introduces a method for determining optimal coordination intervals for multi-robot teams in differentiable motion-planning problems by classifying solutions using second-order properties and solving a Dynamic Coordination Problem (DCP).
- The framework models coordinated behavior as a spectrum between jointly optimal solutions (positive definite full Hessian) and uncoordinated Nash equilibria (positive definite diagonal blocks only).
- The proposed algorithm uses second-order reasoning to identify the value of coordination over time, minimizing a cost function that balances coordination cost and the resulting solution quality.

---

[MVP-LAM: Learning Action-Centric Latent Action via Cross-Viewpoint Reconstruction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03668)

- MVP-LAM (Multi-ViewPoint Latent Action Model): introduces a latent action model trained on time-synchronized multi-view videos using a cross-viewpoint reconstruction objective to learn action-centric discrete latent actions.
- The framework utilizes a frozen DINOv2 visual encoder, a spatiotemporal encoder, and a vector quantizer to generate latent action tokens, which are subsequently used by a spatial decoder for observation feature reconstruction.
- The cross-viewpoint reconstruction objective forces a latent action inferred from one view to predict the future observation in another view, thereby improving action-centricity and boosting downstream manipulation performance when used as pseudo-labels for VLA pretraining.

---

[Mitigating Conversational Inertia in Multi-Turn Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03664)

- CPL (Context Preference Learning): introduces a framework to mitigate conversational inertia in multi-turn LLM agents, utilizing Context Preference Learning (training) and Clip Context (inference) to balance exploration and exploitation.
- CPL calibrates model preferences by fine-tuning the LLM using Direct Preference Optimization on long-short context preference pairs, favoring low-inertia actions generated from shorter contexts over high-inertia actions from longer contexts.
- The Clip Context management strategy periodically clears context history, reducing diagonal attention (conversational inertia) and achieving performance improvements across diverse agentic environments while improving computational efficiency via KV cache reuse.

---

[Search-R2: Enhancing Search-Integrated Reasoning via Actor-Refiner Collaboration](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03647)

- Search-R2: introduces a novel Actor-Refiner collaboration framework that enhances search-integrated reasoning by decomposing the generation process into an Actor and a Meta-Refiner, jointly optimized using Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) and a hybrid reward.
- The Meta-Refiner utilizes a Discriminator to check global coherence and a Trimmer to localize errors, applying a "cut-and-regenerate" mechanism to surgically repair flawed steps and preserve valid reasoning prefixes.
- The system employs a hybrid reward that couples trajectory outcome correctness with a dense process reward quantifying the information density of retrieved evidence, addressing the multi-scale credit assignment problem in RL-optimized LLMs.

[BIRDTurk: Adaptation of the BIRD Text-to-SQL Dataset to Turkish](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03633)

- BIRDTurk Construction Pipeline: introduces BIRDTurk, the first Turkish adaptation of the BIRD Text-to-SQL benchmark, constructed via a controlled, three-phase translation pipeline that preserves logical structure and execution semantics while localizing natural language questions and schema identifiers.
- The pipeline utilizes an LLM (Gemini-2.5-flash) for translation tasks and employs a statistically grounded CLT-based framework for validating large-scale dataset translation quality, achieving 98.15% accuracy on human-evaluated samples.
- Experiments reveal that Turkish introduces consistent performance degradation in Text-to-SQL tasks, which is partially mitigated by agentic multi-stage reasoning pipelines like DIN-SQL, demonstrating stronger cross-lingual robustness.

[Can LLMs Do Rocket Science? Exploring the Limits of Complex Reasoning with GTOC 12](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03630)

- AIDE (Agent for Iterative Data-science Exploration): introduces an evaluation of LLM agents against the complex GTOC 12 astrodynamics challenge, utilizing the adapted MLE-Bench framework, an LLM Agent for solution generation, and an LLM-as-a-Judge for strategic viability scoring, guided by a Tree Search refinement strategy.
- The study finds that while advanced LLMs demonstrate strong conceptual understanding of complex space science tasks, they consistently fail at implementation due to issues like unit inconsistencies and inefficient debugging loops.
- Performance analysis using a 26-point rubric shows that the average strategic viability score of LLMs has nearly doubled in the last two years, indicating rapid improvement in strategic reasoning capabilities.

[Learning Query-Specific Rubrics from Human Preferences for DeepResearch Report Generation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03619)

- MaMs (Multi-agent Markov-state) Workflow with Rubric-Based GRPO: introduces a pipeline to train human-preference-aligned query-specific rubric generators using GRPO with a hybrid reward, and integrates these rubrics into a multi-agent MaMs workflow for DeepResearch report generation.
- The Rubric Generator is trained on a large-scale human preference dataset to produce discriminative and human-aligned supervision signals for DeepResearch agents.
- The MaMs workflow employs specialized Search, State, and Report agents that interact iteratively over an abstract state space to handle long-horizon reasoning and context dependencies inherent in long-form report generation.

[Refer-Agent: A Collaborative Multi-Agent System with Reasoning and Reflection for Referring Video Object Segmentation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03595)

- Refer-Agent: introduces a training-free collaborative multi-agent system for Referring Video Object Segmentation (RVOS), which integrates a Reasoning Pipeline and a Chain-of-Reflection (CoR) mechanism.
- The Reasoning Pipeline uses Coarse-to-Fine frame selection and a Dynamic Focus Layout to enhance visual focus and textual relevance during step-by-step segmentation.
- The CoR mechanism employs Questioner/Responder agents across Existence Reflection and Consistency Reflection stages to verify intermediate results and mitigate LLM hallucinations.

[Understanding and Measuring MCP Behavior under Misleading Tool Descriptions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03580)

- MCPDiFF (automated static analysis framework): introduces a framework to systematically expose and quantify the semantic gap between an MCP Server's claimed tool description and its actual code behavior.
- The framework uses multi-language code parsing and LLMs to analyze semantic features derived from function call chains and repository descriptions, comparing them via vector similarity.
- The study analyzes 10,240 real-world Model Context Protocol (MCP) Servers, finding that approximately 13% exhibit substantial description-code mismatches, posing concrete security risks like undocumented privileged operations.

[Multi-Player, Multi-Strategy Quantum Game Model for Interaction-Aware Decision-Making in Autonomous Driving](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03571)

- QGDM (Quantum Game Decision-Making model): introduces a novel framework for interaction-aware decision-making in autonomous driving, integrating Environment (Simulates driving scenario), Game-Theoretic Modeling (Converts state to normal-form game), Game-Theoretic Solver (Determines optimal action), and Quantum Models (Generates action probabilities).
- The Game-Theoretic Solver uses a multi-step process, prioritizing Strictly Dominant Strategies and Nash Equilibria before resorting to quantum probabilities derived from Quantum Circuits to maximize expected utility.
- QGDM, which runs on standard hardware, significantly improves success rates and reduces collision rates compared to classical game theory approaches in high-interaction scenarios like roundabouts and merging.

---

[SEAD: Self-Evolving Agent for Multi-Turn Service Dialogue](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03548)

- SEAD (Self-Evolving Agent for Service Dialogue): introduces a framework enabling agents to learn effective multi-turn service dialogue strategies without large-scale human annotations, utilizing a Profile Controller, User Role-play Model, Service Agent, Evolving Loop, and Mistake Analysis.
- The framework decouples user modeling into a Profile Controller for curriculum management and a User Role-play Model for realistic simulation, transforming training into a fair adversarial betting game.
- SEAD achieves superior performance in task completion rate and dialogue efficiency compared to LLMs and commercial APIs by employing a self-evolving curriculum based on adaptive difficulty adjustment.

---

[Persona Generators: Generating Diverse Synthetic Personas at Scale](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03545)

- Persona Generators (PG) framework: introduces a methodology for learning Persona Generator functions that maximize diversity in traits, opinions, and preferences across arbitrary contexts, using AlphaEvolve for code optimization.
- The PG function employs a two-stage scalable architecture separating population-level diversity decisions (Autoregressive Stage 1) from per-persona background expansions (Parallel Stage 2) to efficiently generate diverse individuals.
- The system evaluates persona diversity using Concordia simulations and six diversity metrics, demonstrating that evolved generators substantially outperform baselines in coverage and spanning rare trait combinations.

---

[Sequential Linear Contracts on Matroids](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03543)

- OLCPM (Optimal Linear Contract Problem on Matroids): introduces the problem of finding an optimal linear contract between a Principal and an Agent, where the Agent sequentially probes elements subject to costs and structural constraints defined by a Matroid, and the Agent's best response is computed using the FRUGAL Algorithm.
- The research establishes a relationship between OLCPM and UPM (Unreliability Problem on Matroids), showing they are essentially equivalent in terms of exact and approximate solvability, often requiring the addition of parallel copies of elements.
- The paper provides a Fully Polynomial Randomized Approximation Scheme (FPRAS) for OLCPM in two special cases: when non-zero outcomes have roughly balanced expected values, and when the number of outcomes is constant ($m=2$) with zero minimum value.

---

[Group Selection as a Safeguard Against AI Substitution](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03541)

- ABM/EGT Framework: introduces a computational framework to compare AI Complement and AI Substitute strategies regarding their long-term effects on Cumulative Cultural Evolution (CCE) and collective variance.
- The model demonstrates that while the AI Substitute strategy provides higher short-term individual payoffs by reducing learning error and dispersion, the AI Complement strategy, which maintains higher collective variance, is favored under strong cultural group selection.
- The study uses Gumbel distribution to model social learning outcomes and replicator dynamics to analyze the evolutionary stability of AI use strategies in well-mixed and structured populations, informing policy to mitigate cultural collapse risks from widespread GenAI reliance.

---

[Q-Learning for 3D Coverage in VCSEL-based Optical Wireless Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03526)

- Q-LADC: introduces an RL-based framework leveraging Q-learning to autonomously optimize beam divergence angles for dynamic 3D coverage in VCSEL-based Optical Wireless Communication (OWC) systems.
- The framework models the divergence optimization task as a finite-state Markov Decision Process, mapping discrete receiver heights (State Space) to optimal divergence angles (Action Space) by maximizing the spatial coverage Reward Function.
- The resulting lightweight Q-table policy provides near-optimal coverage and real-time adaptability, eliminating the need for analytical modeling or computationally intensive exhaustive search.

---

[A necessary and sufficient condition for discrete-time consensus on star boundaries](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03508)

- DTC-SA: introduces a necessary and sufficient condition for asymptotic consensus of normalized states (directions) in a multi-agent system where agents iteratively update their states on star boundaries using a conical combination of neighbors' states followed by radial projection.
- The algorithm operates on a large class of star boundaries, including $l_p$-spheres, defined by agent-specific directional functions $\gamma_i$, under a directed strongly connected interaction graph.
- The paper demonstrates that when asymptotic consensus of directions occurs, the normalized states converge linearly, and the consensus point is locally continuous in the initial states.

[IntentRL: Training Proactive User-intent Agents for Open-ended Deep Research via Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03468)

- IntentRL: introduces a reinforcement learning framework that trains proactive agents to clarify latent user intent before initiating long-horizon Deep Research tasks, addressing the autonomy-interaction dilemma.
- The framework utilizes a scalable data pipeline based on a Clarification Directed Acyclic Graph (C-DAG) to generate diverse, intent-rich dialogue trajectories from limited seed samples.
- Training employs a two-stage RL strategy, combining offline expert learning (Stage I) with online refinement using an intent-aware user simulator (Stage II) to ensure robustness and adaptive interaction.

[Game-Theoretic and Algorithmic Analyses of Multi-Agent Routing under Crossing Costs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03455)

- CC-MAR: introduces a novel congestion game model for asynchronous multi-agent routing on mixed graphs, where costs are defined by potential head-on encounters (crossing costs) rather than hard constraints.
- The framework provides both game-theoretic results, proving the existence of pure Nash equilibria (PoS=1, PoA unbounded), and algorithmic results addressing the NP-hard minimum-cost solution problem.
- Algorithmic solutions leverage parameterized complexity, yielding FPT and XP results based on structural parameters like the number of arcs, edges, terminal pairs, and vertex cover number.

[HetroD: A High-Fidelity Drone Dataset and Benchmark for Autonomous Driving in Heterogeneous Traffic](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03447)

- HetroD: introduces a high-fidelity drone dataset and benchmark for autonomous driving in heterogeneous traffic, including a Unified Development Toolkit (Converts data formats), Unified Format (Standardized agent-centric data), Motion Planning & RL (Planning and reinforcement learning tasks), Motion Prediction (Forecasting agent trajectories), Traffic Simulation (High-fidelity heterogeneous traffic simulation), and Cross Domain Evaluation (Testing generalization across datasets).
- HetroD comprises over 65.4k high-fidelity agent trajectories, 70% of which are Vulnerable Road Users (VRUs), collected across six topologically diverse, high-traffic urban locations in Taiwan.
- The benchmark reveals that state-of-the-art prediction and planning models struggle with complex VRU behaviors, unstructured maneuvers, and dense multi-agent scenarios, particularly failing to predict lateral VRU movements.

[CRL-VLA: Continual Vision–Language-Action Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03445)

- CRL-VLA (Continual Vision–Language-Action Learning): introduces a continual post-training framework for Vision-Language-Action (VLA) models, utilizing a dual-critic architecture and Goal-Conditioned Value Formulation to balance stability and plasticity.
- The framework achieves asymmetric regulation by constraining the goal-conditioned advantage magnitude on prior tasks via a frozen critic while permitting controlled growth on new tasks via a trainable critic.
- CRL-VLA employs Proximal Policy Optimization (PPO) loss combined with KL regularization and dual value consistency losses to mitigate catastrophic forgetting and enhance forward adaptation.

---

[A-RAG: Scaling Agentic Retrieval-Augmented Generation via Hierarchical Retrieval Interfaces](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03442)

- A-RAG (Agentic Retrieval-Augmented Generation): introduces an agentic RAG framework that exposes hierarchical retrieval interfaces—keyword\_search, semantic\_search, and chunk\_read—to the LLM, enabling autonomous strategy selection and iterative execution for multi-granularity information access.
- Unlike traditional RAG paradigms that rely on single-shot retrieval or predefined workflows, A-RAG allows the LLM agent to dynamically adapt its retrieval strategy based on task characteristics using a ReAct-like agent loop.
- A-RAG consistently outperforms existing Graph-RAG and Workflow RAG methods across diverse QA benchmarks while demonstrating efficient test-time scaling behavior and superior context efficiency.

[Ontology-to-tools compilation for executable semantic constraint enforcement in LLM agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03439)

- Ontology-to-tools compilation framework: introduces a mechanism for coupling LLM agents with formal domain knowledge by compiling ontological specifications (T-Box) into executable tool interfaces (MCP servers) for knowledge graph construction.
- The framework enables LLM agents (Instantiation Agent) to enforce semantic constraints during knowledge graph instance creation through iterative tool invocation and structured feedback on constraint violations.
- The approach is demonstrated on metal-organic polyhedra synthesis literature within The World Avatar ecosystem, yielding grounded, ontology-consistent knowledge graphs covering synthesis steps and chemical entities.

[FAILURE IS FEEDBACK: History-Aware Backtracking for Agentic Traversal in Multimodal Graphs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03432)

- FIF (FAILURE IS FEEDBACK): introduces an LLM-driven agentic retriever that models open-domain multimodal retrieval as a sequential decision process over a layered component graph, utilizing a history-aware backtracking mechanism and cost-aware strategy escalation.
- The system employs an Orchestrator that dynamically chooses among TRAVERSE, PLAN, and STOP actions based on a structured memory recording accumulated evidence and explicit success/failure outcomes.
- History-aware backtracking leverages failure traces to re-anchor the search to promising prior contexts and revise subqueries, enhancing robustness and efficiency in multihop navigation.

[ProAct: A Benchmark and Multimodal Framework for Structure-Aware Proactive Response](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03430)

- ProAct-Helper: introduces a multimodal framework for structure-aware proactive response, built on an MLLM, HBM (Cross-level semantic consistency), Task Graph (Structural grounding/constraints), Perception Pipeline (Trigger/Task/Step/Future detection), and Entropy-driven Heuristic Search (Action selection/parallelization).
- The framework leverages explicit task graphs (DAGs) encoding step dependencies and parallel execution possibilities to guide action selection and enable concurrent progress.
- The paper also introduces ProAct-75, a benchmark for vision-based proactive response across assistance, maintenance, and safety monitoring scenarios, featuring 91,581 step-level annotations.

---

[SWE-World: Building Software Engineering Agents in Docker-Free Environments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03419)

- SWE-World: introduces a Docker-free framework that replaces resource-intensive physical execution environments with LLM-based learned surrogates for training and evaluating software engineering agents, including a Code Agent, Lightweight Sandbox, SWE-World Transition Model, SWE-World Reward Model, and Context.
- The framework separates agent actions into lightweight operations handled deterministically by the Sandbox and code execution actions approximated by the LLM-based SWT and SWR models.
- Experiments demonstrate that agents trained entirely with Docker-free execution feedback achieve performance comparable to or better than Docker-based pipelines, significantly improving scalability for supervised fine-tuning and reinforcement learning.

---

[Socratic-Geo: Synthetic Data Generation and Geometric Reasoning via Multi-Agent Interaction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03414)

- Socratic-Geo: introduces a fully autonomous framework for goal-driven geometric data synthesis, utilizing Teacher, Solver, and Generator agents in a closed-loop interaction.
- The Teacher uses the Reflect-RePI pipeline to programmatically invent new problems based on the Solver's failure paths, ensuring geometric validity and targeted curriculum evolution.
- The Socratic-Solver achieves state-of-the-art geometric reasoning performance using only a quarter of baseline data, while the Socratic-Generator sets a new open-source standard for text-to-image generation.

---

[Verified Critical Step Optimization for LLM Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03412)

- CSO (Critical Step Optimization): introduces a post-training approach that focuses preference learning on verified critical steps identified in failed policy trajectories where alternative actions demonstrably flip task outcomes from failure to success.
- The method uses a Process Reward Model (PRM) to identify candidate critical steps and leverages an Expert Model to propose high-quality alternatives, which are then verified via branch rollouts using the Policy Model.
- CSO constructs fine-grained, verifiable preference data for targeted Direct Preference Optimization (DPO) training, achieving superior performance and sample efficiency compared to trajectory-level or dense step-level methods.

---

[SWE-Master: Unleashing the Potential of Software Engineering Agents via Post-Training](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03411)

- SWE-Master: introduces an open-source post-training framework for software engineering agents, including teacher-trajectory synthesis, data filtering, long-horizon SFT, RL with real execution feedback, and an inference framework design featuring IDE-level code navigation (lsp_tool).
- The approach achieves a 61.4% resolve rate on SWE-bench Verified using Qwen2.5-Coder-32B, substantially outperforming existing open-source baselines, and reaches 70.8% with Test-Time Scaling (TTS@8).
- SWE-Master integrates a Language Server Protocol (LSP)-based tool (lsp_tool) at inference time to provide IDE-level code comprehension and structured repository navigation, significantly improving agent efficiency.

---

[Feasible strategies for conflict resolution within intuitionistic fuzzy preference-based conflict situations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03403)

- IFPS-based model: introduces intuitionistic fuzzy preference-based conflict situations (IFPS) and measures to characterize agents' attitudes towards issue pairs with finer granularity than classical models.
- The framework develops three-way conflict analysis models to trisect agent pairs, the agent set, and the issue set using thresholds calculated via relative loss functions based on Bayesian minimum risk theory.
- Feasible strategies for conflict resolution are constructed using an iterative adjustment mechanism that minimizes the conflict degree and the magnitude of preference adjustments via optimization.

---

[PlanTRansformer: Unified Prediction and Planning with Goal-conditioned Transformer](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03376)

- Plan TRansformer (PTR): introduces a unified Gaussian Mixture Transformer framework that integrates goal-conditioned prediction, dynamic feasibility, collision avoidance, and lane-level topology reasoning to bridge the prediction-planning asymmetry in autonomous driving.
- PTR extends prediction models by incorporating planning constraints through differentiable losses and goal-conditioned reasoning via high-level commands and reachable lane information.
- A teacher-student training strategy progressively masks surrounding agent commands to align training with inference conditions where agent intentions are unavailable, improving generalization and performance.

---

[The Intervention Paradox: Accurate Failure Prediction in Agents Does Not Imply Effective Failure Prevention](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03338)

- Disruption-Recovery Framework: introduces a pre-deployment test to evaluate proactive LLM critic-based intervention by quantifying the disruption-recovery tradeoff using baseline failure rate ($p$), recovery rate ($r$), and disruption rate ($d$).
- The research demonstrates that high LLM critic accuracy alone is insufficient, as intervention often degrades performance in high-success regimes by disrupting successful trajectories, especially through early-step interventions.
- The framework provides a deployment guideline based on the intervention threshold $p^* = d/(r+d)$, correctly predicting when intervention will help (low-success tasks) or harm (high-success tasks).

---

[MedSAM-Agent: Empowering Interactive Medical Image Segmentation with Multi-turn Agentic Reinforcement Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03320)

- MedSAM-Agent: introduces a framework that reformulates interactive medical image segmentation as a multi-step autonomous decision-making process, utilizing a Visual Agent (MLLM decision-making) and a Segmentation Tool (Interactive mask generation) trained via a Two-stage Training Pipeline (Initial capability/Refinement optimization) guided by a Clinical-Fidelity Process Reward Design (Interaction protocol adherence/Segmentation accuracy/Monotonic quality gains/Efficient termination/Procedural efficiency).
- The framework employs a Hybrid Prompting Strategy to generate expert-curated trajectories, enabling the agent to internalize human-like decision heuristics and adaptive refinement strategies using both bounding boxes and points.
- The two-stage training pipeline integrates Supervised Fine-Tuning for initial capability with Reinforcement Learning using verifiable, process-aware rewards to promote interaction parsimony and achieve state-of-the-art performance across six medical modalities.

---

[MIRROR: A Multi-Agent Framework with Iterative Adaptive Revision and Hierarchical Retrieval for Optimization Modeling in Operations Research](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03318)

- MIRROR: introduces a fine-tuning-free, end-to-end multi-agent framework that translates natural language optimization problems into mathematical models and executable solver code, utilizing Parameter Extraction-, Modeling Advisor-, Mathematical Modeling-, Code Generation-, Modeling Revision- and Code Revision-agents, Iterative Adaptive Revision, Hierarchical Retrieval-Augmented Generation, Dual Memory, Executor, and an Exemplar Library.
- The framework operates in a closed-loop paradigm (Analysis, Modeling, Implementation, Revision), ensuring correctness and robustness through execution-driven self-correction and dynamic external knowledge infusion.
- The Iterative Adaptive Revision (IAR) mechanism leverages local memory to store historical outputs and revision tips, enabling collaborative error diagnosis and refinement by specialized revision agents upon execution failure.

---

[MEMORA: A Harmonic Memory Representation Balancing Abstraction and Specificity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03315)

- MEMORA (Harmonic Memory Representation): introduces a memory architecture that structurally balances abstraction and specificity using Primary Abstraction (canonical identity), Memory Value (concrete information), Cue Anchors (contextual access points), and Policy-Driven Memory Retrieval (active reasoning process).
- The architecture organizes information into Memory Entries linked to Episodic Memory, forming an Implicit Memory Graph that supports relational reasoning and temporal coherence.
- Retrieval is formulated as a Markov Decision Process guided by an Action Policy (RE-QUERY, EXPAND, STOP), which can be optimized using Group-Relative Policy Updates (GRPO).

---

[Scaling In-Context Online Learning Capability of LLMs via Cross-Episode Meta-RL](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04089)

- ORBIT (Online Reinforcement-Based In-Context Training): introduces a multi-task, multi-episode meta-reinforcement learning framework that trains a pretrained LLM agent ($\pi_{\theta}$) using Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) to maximize trajectory-level reward based on persistent interaction history stored in the context window across diverse Task MDPs.
- The framework enables the LLM agent to perform in-context online learning and adaptation in entirely unseen environments without parameter updates at inference time, matching GPT-5.2 performance.
- ORBIT induces an exploration-exploitation trade-off across episodes, allowing the agent to gather task-relevant information in early trials and exploit the learned mental model in later trials for reliable execution.

---

[Agentic AI-Empowered Dynamic Survey Framework](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04071)

- Agentic AI-Empowered Dynamic Survey Framework (DSF): introduces a framework that reframes survey writing as a long-horizon maintenance problem, supporting continuous updating of existing surveys by incrementally integrating new work using specialized LLM-based agents.
- The DSF utilizes a persistent survey state with a frozen structure ($C$) and conservative update constraints to minimize disruption and prevent cumulative drift over time.
- The framework employs a multi-agent architecture, including planning-, routing-, and synthesis-agents, to enforce localized updates and maintain factual accuracy and topical coherence.

---

[A Consensus-Bayesian Framework for Detecting Malicious Activity in Enterprise Directory Access Graphs](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04027)

- Consensus-Bayesian Framework (CBF): introduces a consensus-based Bayesian framework to detect malicious user behavior in enterprise directory access graphs, utilizing the Multi-Level Interaction Graph G(W, C'), Directory-Level Graph G[W], User-User Dependency Graph G[C_i], SCC Decomposition Pipeline, Opinion Dynamics Simulation, and Bayesian Anomaly Scoring Mechanism, which simulates access evolution using influence-weighted opinion dynamics.
- The framework leverages multi-level graph structures and opinion dynamics theory to model normal behavior and detect deviations indicative of potential security threats by monitoring the evolution of logical dependency matrices $C_i$ and the shared influence matrix $W$.
- Anomalies are detected proactively by observing abrupt structural changes, deviations from expected user consensus, or persistent disagreements, quantified using scaled opinion variance and an online Bayesian update mechanism.

---

[FDA Flocking: Future Direction-Aware Flocking via Velocity Prediction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04012)

- FDA (Future Direction-Aware Flocking): introduces a bio-inspired anticipatory augmentation of reactive flocking, blending reactive alignment with a predictive term based on short-term estimates of neighbors' future velocities, regulated by a tunable blending parameter.
- The predictive structure enhances velocity consensus and cohesion-separation balance while mitigating adverse effects of sensing and communication delays and measurement noise that destabilize purely reactive baselines.
- Simulations demonstrate that FDA achieves faster and higher alignment, enhanced translational displacement, and improved robustness compared to purely reactive models, supporting deployment in aerial robotic swarms.

---

[After Talking with 1,000 Personas: Learning Preference-Aligned Proactive Assistants From Large-Scale Persona Interactions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.04000)

- Two-Stage Personalization Framework: introduces a population-to-individual learning pipeline for preference-aligned proactive assistants that uses LLM-driven simulation to learn shared preference structure and lightweight on-device steering for individual adaptation.
- Stage 1 uses Supervised Fine-Tuning on a large synthetic dataset of 1,000 census-aligned personas to train a compact 3B Population Model, establishing a strong cold start without relying on real user logs.
- Stage 2 adapts the assistant to individual users entirely on-device using Activation Vector Steering, which modifies internal activations based on simple interaction feedback signals across five preference dimensions (timing, autonomy, communication style, context adaptation, and domain prioritization).

---

[Dynamic Matching Under Patience Imbalance](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03995)

- Dynamic Matching System: introduces a dynamic matching problem on a two-sided platform with unbalanced patience, characterizing the optimal centralized policy and the welfare-maximizing decentralized equilibrium using threshold rules.
- The model features long-lived supply agents incurring waiting costs and short-lived demand agents who depart if unmatched, both differentiated into H-type and L-type quality levels.
- The decentralized system can be perfectly coordinated with the centralized optimum by tuning the matching payoff allocation proportion ($\alpha$), a result contrasting with full-backlog systems.

---

[Active Epistemic Control for Query-Efficient Verified Planning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03974)

- AEC (Active Epistemic Control): introduces an epistemic-categorical planning layer that unifies learned prediction with grounded verification, utilizing a Grounded Fact Store, a Belief Store, a Predictive Model Interface, an Epistemic Controller, a Query Macro-Action, and a Sound Verifier.
- AEC maintains a strict separation between grounded facts (used for commitment) and model beliefs (used only for pruning candidate plans) to ensure feasibility is certified only by external evidence.
- The Epistemic Controller decides whether to query the environment or simulate predictions based on uncertainty and ambiguity margins, achieving competitive success with reduced replanning rounds compared to strong LLM-agent baselines.

---

[AgentArk: Distilling Multi-Agent Intelligence into a Single LLM Agent](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03955)

- AgentArk: introduces a novel framework to distill multi-agent dynamics into a single LLM agent, utilizing Multi-Agent Debate, Knowledge Extraction, and Hierarchical Distillation via R-SFT, DA, and PAD.
- The framework shifts the computational burden from inference to training, enabling the single LLM to achieve strong reasoning and self-correction capabilities efficiently while maintaining robustness and generalization.
- Process-Aware Distillation (PAD) uses a Process Reward Model (PRM) and Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) to internalize the iterative critique-and-revision dynamics of multi-agent debates into the student LLM.

---

[Learning Multi-type heterogeneous interacting particle systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03954)

- Three-Stage Joint Inference Framework: introduces a novel approach for the joint inference of network topology, multi-type interaction kernels, and latent type assignments in heterogeneous interacting particle systems from multi-trajectory data.
- The framework addresses the challenging non-convex mixed-integer optimization problem by decoupling it into a low-rank matrix sensing stage, a geometric clustering stage, and a final matrix factorization and post-processing stage.
- Theoretical guarantees are provided, including estimation error bounds under a Restricted Isometry Property (RIP) assumption and conditions for exact recovery of interaction types based on cluster separability.

---

[Enhancing Mathematical Problem Solving in LLMs through Execution-Driven Reasoning Augmentation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03950)

- IIPC (Iteratively Improved Program Construction): introduces an execution-guided reasoning methodology that iteratively refines programmatic reasoning chains using execution feedback and a dual-branch architecture to enhance mathematical problem solving in LLMs.
- The framework utilizes a dual-branch architecture consisting of a program refinement branch for iterative code correction and a token-level reasoning branch ($f_{cot}$) for context-stable Chain-of-Thought generation.
- IIPC maintains a persistent Error Descriptor Memory ($M_t$) to log past mistakes, guiding the refinement process to avoid repeating unsuccessful strategies and stabilize reasoning trajectories.

---

[Autonomous AI Agents for Real-Time Affordable Housing Site Selection: Multi-Objective Reinforcement Learning Under Regulatory Constraints](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03940)

- AURA (Autonomous Urban Resource Allocator): introduces a novel multi-agent reinforcement learning system for real-time affordable housing site selection, including a Coordination Agent (orchestration), Geospatial Analysis Agent (GNN encoding), Regulatory Compliance Agent (constraint satisfaction), Multi-Objective Optimization Agent (PC-PPO execution), and Execution Agent (portfolio construction).
- The system formalizes site selection as a Constrained Multi-Objective Markov Decision Process (CMO-MDP) optimizing four objectives (accessibility, environment, cost, equity) subject to 127 hard regulatory constraints.
- AURA achieved 94.3% regulatory compliance and 37.2% Pareto hypervolume improvement, reducing site selection time from 18 months to 72 hours in a New York City deployment case study.

---

[C-IDS: Solving Contextual POMDP via Information-Directed Objective](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03939)

- C-IDS (Contextual Information-Directed Sampling): introduces a policy synthesis algorithm for Contextual Partially Observable Markov Decision Processes (CPOMDPs) by maximizing an Information-Directed Objective, optimized using a Variational Policy Gradient method, implemented with an LSTM-based Policy Network and an Extended Kalman Filter Inference Mechanism, within a CPOMDP Environment using a Simulator.
- The Information-Directed Objective augments reward maximization with a mutual information regularizer between the latent context and the agent's observations to jointly optimize task performance and context inference.
- C-IDS achieves a sublinear Bayesian regret bound and demonstrates faster context identification and higher returns compared to standard POMDP solvers in continuous Light-Dark environments.

---

#### 2nd February 2026

[RLAnything: Forge Environment, Policy, and Reward Model in Completely Dynamic RL System](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02488)

- RLAnything: introduces a dynamic closed-loop RL framework that jointly optimizes the Environment Model (Dynamic Adaptation), Policy Model (Trained via Integrated Feedback), and Reward Model (Optimized via Consistency Feedback) to amplify learning signals.
- The framework uses integrated feedback combining verifiable outcome rewards and step-wise signals for policy training, while the reward model is optimized using consistency feedback based on outcome and self-consistency.
- Environment adaptation is automatically driven by critic feedback from both the policy and reward models, enabling targeted adjustment of task difficulty to benefit both models and strengthen the overall system.

---

[RE-TRAC: REcursive TRAjectory Compression for Deep Search Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02486)

- RE-TRAC (REcursive TRAjectory Compression): introduces an agentic framework that performs cross-trajectory exploration by recursively compressing previous trajectories into a structured state representation to condition subsequent rollouts.
- This framework moves beyond the linear ReAct paradigm by enabling iterative reflection, globally informed planning, and systematic exploration of previously incomplete branches, significantly reducing redundant tool calls and token usage.
- The core mechanism utilizes a structured state representation encompassing accumulated evidence, analytical conclusions, and uncertainties, leading to consistent performance gains of 15-20% over ReAct on BrowseComp.

---

[AGENTRY: Diagnosing AI Agent Failures from Execution Trajectories](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02475)

- AGENTRX: introduces a domain-agnostic diagnostic framework that pinpoints the critical failure step and category in a failed agent trajectory by synthesizing and evaluating constraints step-by-step, producing an auditable validation log, which an LLM-based judge uses for root-cause attribution.
- The framework utilizes both Global Constraints (derived from tool schema and domain policy) and Dynamic Constraints (trajectory-specific rules) to enforce correctness over agent executions.
- The authors introduce AGENTRX, a novel benchmark of 115 failed agent trajectories across three domains (API workflows, incident management, web/file tasks), annotated with critical failure steps and a grounded-theory derived cross-domain failure taxonomy.

---

[MemSkill: Learning and Evolving Memory Skills for Self-Evolving Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02474)

- MemSkill: reframes memory operations as learnable and evolvable memory skills, using a Controller to select a Top-K set of skills and an LLM Executor to generate skill-guided memories, all within a closed-loop optimization process.
- The system employs a Designer that periodically analyzes representative failure cases mined from a Hard Case Buffer to refine existing skills and propose new ones, thereby evolving the shared Skill Bank.
- This span-level, skill-conditioned generation approach, optimized via reinforcement learning and LLM-guided evolution, improves task performance and generalization across conversational and embodied interactive benchmarks.

---

[Avenir-Web: Human-Experience-Imitating Multimodal Web Agents with Mixture of Grounding Experts](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02468)

- Avenir-Web: introduces a web agent that achieves open-source state-of-the-art performance on the ONLINE-MIND2WEB benchmark by integrating EIP, MoGE, Task-Tracking Checklist, and Adaptive Memory for resilient long-horizon web execution.
- The framework utilizes a decoupled strategic planning and execution loop to overcome element grounding, procedural knowledge, and unstable long-term memory bottlenecks in complex web environments.
- MoGE prioritizes visual-first grounding using MLLMs, falling back to semantic structural reasoning for complex elements, while Adaptive Memory uses Chunked Recursive Summarization to maintain strategic situational awareness.

---

[Relationship-Aware Hierarchical 3D Scene Graph for Task Reasoning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02456)

- REASONINGGRAPH: introduces a framework for incrementally constructing a reasoning-enhanced hierarchical 3D scene graph that integrates open-vocabulary features and supports object-relational reasoning across five abstraction levels.
- The approach leverages a VLM to infer object relationship features and combines LLMs and a VLM in a task reasoning module to interpret natural language tasks and assess object-interaction feasibility.
- The hierarchical 3D scene graph structure includes layers for Metric-Semantic Mesh ($L_1$), Objects ($L_2$), Places ($L_3$), Rooms ($L_4$), and Buildings ($L_5$), enabling context-aware understanding for autonomous agents.

---

[DRIFT-BENCH : Diagnosing Cooperative Breakdowns in LLM Agents under Input Faults via Multi-Turn Interaction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.02455)

- DRIFT-BENCH: introduces a diagnostic benchmark evaluating LLM agents' pragmatic recovery under systematic input faults via multi-turn clarification across state-oriented and service-oriented execution environments.
- The benchmark employs a theoretically grounded taxonomy of four input faults (intention, premise, parameter, expression) and a persona-driven LLM-as-User simulator to test agent resilience.
- Evaluation using the RISE protocol reveals a "Clarification Paradox" where multi-turn interaction degrades performance in opaque black-box systems due to context overload and execution bias.

---

#### 1st February 2026

[WebSentinel: Detecting and Localizing Prompt Injection Attacks for Web Agents](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.03792)

- WebSentinel: introduces a two-step approach for detecting and localizing prompt injection attacks in webpages, including a Step I (Extraction) using an Extractor LLM and Code Pattern Matching, and a Step II (Detection and Localization) using an Analyzer LLM and Alignment Checks.
- Step I utilizes Untargeted Pruning and Targeted Pruning strategies to reduce the input size for the Analyzer LLM while preserving necessary contextual cues from the webpage.
- The Analyzer LLM performs General and Type-specific Alignment Checks on the extracted segments of interest within the context of the surrounding webpage to minimize false positives and enhance detection accuracy.

---

[Ethology of Latent Spaces](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.05710)

- ELS: questions the neutrality of VLM latent spaces by proposing an ethological approach to analyze their algorithmic behaviors, revealing specific algorithmic sensitivities across OpenAI CLIP, OpenCLIP/LAION, and SigLIP models.
- The research introduces three operational concepts: computational latent politicization, emergent bias, and three algorithmic scopic regimes (entropic, institutional, semiotic) to characterize distinct modes of structuring the visible.
- Comparative analysis using bipolar semantic axes demonstrates significant inter-model divergences in attributing political and cultural categories to artworks, confirming that metric/semantic equivalence is locally unstable and corpus-dependent.

---
